Shocking News: White Paper Used Instead of Banknotes

Each Bundle of Banknotes Had Only One Real Banknote on Top, the Rest Was White Paper

A Total Shortage of 42,305 Yuan

—The Main Culprit, Hua Zhongchu, Flees to Hong Kong with Two Prostitutes—

The China Agricultural and Industrial Bank at 348 Henan Road issues banknotes. Qian Zhuang (money shops) that do business with the bank and want banknotes of a consistent style can exchange their various banknotes for the bank's uniform banknotes. On the 12th of this month, the Jiuru Qian Zhuang on Huade Road in Hongkou sent an old clerk to the Agricultural and Industrial Bank with 16,000 yuan in miscellaneous banknotes. After the bank's staff checked them, they took out three large bundles and one small bundle of banknotes from the banknote storage room, saying that the large bundles each contained 5,000 yuan and the small bundle contained 1,000 yuan, all in 10-yuan denominations. The old clerk then opened the bundles to count them, but unexpectedly, in each bundle, only the top banknote was a genuine 10-yuan note, and the rest were blank pieces of paper without a single word on them. He immediately returned them all. The bank staff was shocked to see this. They re-counted the amount and handed it over to the old clerk to take back. The bank manager was informed and appointed staff to go to the banknote storage room and carefully check each bundle of banknotes, and found many bundles with the above-mentioned fraudulent situation. The total shortage was as high as 42,305 yuan. The banknote storage room was staffed by five clerks and three trainees who were responsible for managing and checking the banknotes. After the incident, Hua Zhongchu, one of the five clerks, had disappeared. The other four, Ding Chengfu from Pudong, Pan Ruilin from Suzhou, Zhu Minggui from Jiangbei, and Ding Hao, were under serious suspicion. Later, the bank manager reported to the General Inspectorate, which sent Detective Zhang Mingde to investigate. The four, Ding, and others were arrested at 6 p.m. the previous evening, and they were asked about Hua Zhongchu's whereabouts. According to Ding, Hua Zhongchu had been spending lavishly recently, opening room 224 at the Yangtze Hotel as a pleasure den and also frequenting prostitutes, forming an inseparable bond with Yinghong the Second and Yinghong the Third at the Yinghong Shuyu in Huile Lane, Guangxi Road. Detective Zhang believed that Hua might still be indulging in hotels and brothels, and immediately went to the two places to investigate. It was then learned that Hua had taken this pair of sisters and boarded a ship of the Dale Yanghang at 4 p.m. the day before, fleeing to Hong Kong. Detective Zhang then asked the captain to send a telegram to the British authorities in Hong Kong, asking them to conduct a thorough search when the ship arrived in Hong Kong and to detain Hua and the two prostitutes if found, and to reply by telegram so that they could be brought back. Yesterday morning, Ding, Pan, Zhu, and Ding were sent to the First Special District Court. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, described the course of events and requested that Ding et al. be handed over to the police for detention pending a detailed investigation and the return of the fugitive before proceeding with the prosecution. Judge Qian of the court questioned Ding et al. briefly and ordered them to be detained pending further questioning.

Four Unemployed Overseas Chinese from Vladivostok Repatriated

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning on the Bingfa Wheel

Public Security Bureau Finding Ways to Send Them Home

Song Shaoxian, a 21-year-old from Laiyang County, Shandong Province, was unemployed at home in the 16th year of the Republic of China and could not make a living. He traveled to Vladivostok by ship with his mother, Song Ji (40 years old), to work. At the same time, fellow villagers Guan Fuchen (58 years old) and Dong Xiyan (70 years old), from Yexian County, Shandong Province, also worked in Vladivostok. After eight years, they were affected by the recent economic downturn there, and there was no work to do, so they were unemployed and destitute. As a result, they were stranded in a foreign country and had difficulty finding food and lodging. Song and the other three reported to the Chinese Consul General in Vladivostok, requesting assistance in repatriation. After receiving the report, the consul considered it pitiful that the overseas Chinese were stranded in a foreign country and prepared a document to send Song Shaoxian and the other three men and women back to China. They boarded a French ship on the 8th of this month, departing from Vladivostok, and arrived in Shanghai at about 8 a.m. yesterday morning. After landing, they presented the document to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, requesting assistance. The bureau instructed the relief section to summon the case, interrogate each person's name and register the case, and then sent Song Shaoxian and others to the Xintai Hotel in the 16th block of Nanshi for temporary accommodation, and will repatriate them to their original home in Shandong.

In an Instant, the Iron Box Disappeared

The Central Bank Quickly Solves the Case

Prompt Search Finds the Stolen Silver Intact

—Chef Li Zhengyin Sentenced to Two Months—

The Runfeng Qian Zhuang stored 16,500 yuan in banknotes in an iron box at 2 p.m. the day before yesterday and sent apprentice He Wenkui to the Central Bank outside the Concession to exchange them for silver. After arriving at the bank, while he and other staff members were taking out the banknotes from the box to check them, the iron box suddenly disappeared in an instant. However, only 4,500 yuan of banknotes had been taken out of the box, and most of them remained. The apprentice panicked and immediately asked the doorman and patrolman of the bank, but they had not seen anyone carrying the box out. They realized that the stolen goods were still in the bank. The patrolman immediately searched the bank and found the original box under the bed in the bedroom of Li Zhengyin, a Yangzhou chef in the bank. The remaining 12,000 yuan of banknotes in the box were also intact. The patrolman reported to the General Inspectorate, which sent Chinese and Western detectives to arrest Li. The Central Bank exchanged the original stolen money for silver and handed it over to He Wenkui to take back to Runfeng. Yesterday morning, the police summoned witnesses and sent Li to the First Special District Court. Judge Zhan Liangce opened the court to interrogate him. Police lawyer Chen Ming explained the course of the case and requested that the defendant be punished for theft. Chen Zongguang and He Wenkui, staff members of the Central Bank, testified to the situation at the time. When questioned, the defendant Li Zhengyin could not deny that the stolen goods were found in his bedroom, but denied that he stole and hid the box, saying that he did not know who put it under his bed. After reviewing the confession, Judge Zhan sentenced Li to two months in prison as a warning.

The Shanghai South Public Bus Management Office Increases Special Buses for the Longhua Incense Fair

Scheduled to Start on the First Day of Next Month

New Routes Will Be Opened at the Same Time

The Shanghai South Public Bus Management Office of the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities has ordered more than 20 large Montane light buses from the United States to develop traffic in Nanshi. New routes will be opened on March 1. The details are as follows: The Shanghai South Public Bus Management Office is adding vehicles to the Longhua Incense Fair route, as the number of buses on the original Route 1 will not be enough to handle the expected traffic during the upcoming Incense Fair this year. The large Montane carriages are now being fitted overnight, and it is expected that they will be completed by the end of this month and will start operating on the first day of next month.

New routes will be opened at the same time. Shanghai South Public Buses currently only have Route 1, the Longhua Line, and Route 2, the half-circular city route. In order to develop traffic, two new routes have been specially opened: (1) from Xieqiao via Ximen to Zhaojiabang Road and the 16th block; (2) from Xieqiao along Lujiabang Road to the Hugunjunying, via Limalu and Banchengyuan Road to Xieqiao as the terminus. These two routes will start operating on March 1 at the same time.

Morning: Public Concession in Good Health

According to the Public Works Department's health officer's work report for the previous year, although the summer was unusually hot and there was a lack of rain, there were generally not many major infectious diseases. In terms of mortality rate, the foreign rate was 11.43 per thousand, which is comparable to that of major cities around the world. However, the foreign population in Shanghai has fewer elderly and infirm people, which is also a reason for the low mortality rate. The mortality rate for Chinese residents was 14.25 per thousand, which is also not high. However, this record is not reliable and there are factors that cannot be managed, so it cannot be used as a basis.

Cholera Is Almost Non-Existent: Cholera has hardly occurred in the morning. This phenomenon has continued for two years. Since its historical cyclical nature has not been broken, it is unlikely to break out on a large scale this year, but it is difficult to say. However, smallpox was quite prevalent in January and March, reaching a high of 21 cases in one week. There were also many gastrointestinal diseases such as typhoid fever and dysentery. Typhoid fever vaccinations have been carried out for several years, but they do not seem to be very effective and need to be further prevented. As for dysentery, it will not be easy to stop it until there is great progress in sanitation outside the concession and effective measures are taken to disinfect food. New methods have been tried for fly control, which may be effective. This requires long-term effort.

Physical Examination of School Children: The general work of the Health Department this year has been quite calm, but the physical examination of school students is a new initiative. It has started with the municipal Chinese schools. The preliminary survey found many cases of trachoma and other infectious diseases, and prevention was immediately carried out. The cost is small, but it can avoid future transmission and the gains are huge.

Milk Disinfection and Inspection: The Milk Investigation Committee's research concluded that all [B] grade milk and cheese should be compulsorily disinfected. Shanghai's weather is warmer and milk is more likely to be dangerous, so disinfection is necessary. Due to the development and competition in the dairy industry, prices will not increase. The unprecedented development of dairy factories is due to the increasing number of Chinese people who drink milk, but the effectiveness of supervision is also important. Because the loss of dairy cows with infectious diseases in Shanghai is quite large, attention has been paid to the isolation of cattle. The dairy farmers are very willing to cooperate, and it seems that the prevention has been slightly effective. In addition, regulations have been drafted for the import of cattle from other ports, and they will be implemented after the National Government promulgates measures to achieve consistency.

Further Promotion of Hospitals: There has been no major expansion of hospitals this year. The fever hospital in the western district will not be able to start construction until 1935. Accommodation for the mentally ill is becoming increasingly difficult, but the mental hospital has been slightly modified, and the Bureau has also provided subsidies for the construction of a new charitable hospital in Minhang, which may slightly relieve concerns in this area. As for the equipment for general diseases, the construction of the Medical Investigation Committee has been further studied in detail. The Health Department believes that it is possible to set up needed clinics at any time, and to subsidize the corresponding hospitals, so that they can reserve some beds in the concession. This idea has been approved by the board of directors.

Special Research on Hookworm Disease: Due to a doctor's raising the issue of whether hookworm disease is transmitted to children through parks, a detailed study has been conducted. However, the investigation is difficult to start. Only a few park employees were found to have the disease, but this is also a normal phenomenon. Mass treatment has now been carried out and will be observed again. In addition, attention has been paid to preventing the risk of transmission from outside the park, but it is difficult to prevent children from walking barefoot in the countryside.

The Zoo Purchases a Large Whale to Make a Specimen for Permanent Display

Weighing More Than Ten Tons, Immense

The Municipal Zoo recently purchased a huge whale from Chongming, which was loaded onto a wheel and transported to Shanghai on the 4th of this month. It is now stored at the specimen manufacturing center in Gaochang Temple. A reporter from Dagong News visited the center yesterday. The whale is 41 feet long, its abdomen is 16 feet in circumference and 7 feet wide, its mouth is 8 feet long, its flat head occupies almost one-third of its body, its eyes are small, its tail is flat, it has no hind fins, it has nostrils on top, its back is black, and its abdomen has cloud patterns. It weighs more than ten tons, which is immense. However, it died after being taken out of the water. The specimen manufacturing center is now removing the whale meat to make a full-size skeleton specimen. The weight of the whale skin and bones still reaches five tons. The whale's skeleton will likely be finished within a month and will be displayed in the Municipal Zoo for the public to view.

The Soviet Special Ship for Welcoming Mei, the Sif, Has Arrived in Shanghai

Stopping in Pudong to Load Chinese Tea

Will Not Depart Until Three Days Later

The Soviet government specially sent a special ship to Shanghai to welcome Mei Lanfang and others to Russia. The Greek ship that was sent first was replaced with the Sif ship from the Soviet Russian merchant fleet due to the poor quality of its cabins. The ship has arrived in Shanghai and is now loading goods. The details are as follows:

Arriving in Shanghai to Unload Cargo

The S.S. Sever, the special ship sent by the Soviet government to China to welcome Dr. Mei Lanfang and others to Russia, arrived in Shanghai from Vladivostok yesterday morning. Because the ship contained Russian goods that needed to be unloaded in Pudong, it immediately berthed at the Swire Company's Huatong Wharf. Unloading began yesterday at noon.

Welcoming Mr. Mei

The Sif ship is the best passenger ship in the Soviet merchant fleet, originally sailing in Europe. This time, it was dispatched to China by order of the Soviet government to transport Mei Lanfang and his party. The Soviet Association in Shanghai is responsible for all reception arrangements on board. After the ship arrived in Shanghai yesterday, the association sent personnel to the ship to discuss everything with the captain.

Loading Tea Bricks

In addition to welcoming Dr. Mei and his party, the Sif ship is transporting a large batch of tea bricks, a total of 40,000 bags, to Russia, first to Vladivostok, then to Moscow. The ship has already started loading these tea bricks. According to the personnel managing the ship, the Sif ship will take about three days to load all the tea, so Dr. Mei's departure from Shanghai will be three days after the tea is loaded.

Municipal Zoo Plans to Purchase New and Exotic Animals

Polar Bears, Rhinos, Zebras, Sea Lions, Orangutans, and Other Animals

More Than Ten Thousand People Visited on the 5th

The Shanghai Municipal Zoo on Wenmiao Road in Shanghai has been very popular with visitors recently during the New Year period. On the 5th of this month (i.e., the second day of the lunar New Year), the number of visitors reached 15,766. According to Shen Xiangrui, the director of the zoo, the zoo plans to add polar bears, rhinos, and other animals. The details are as follows:

Preparing to Purchase Animals

The zoo recently added two bird sheds, one to the right of the ticket office and one between the eagle shed and the hibiscus bird shed. They have now been fully completed and are scheduled to open this week. One of these bird sheds is for raising golden pheasants, ring-necked pheasants, and other pheasants. These pheasants were originally in the same shed as the cranes. However, the crane platform is in the water, and these pheasants are not accustomed to living in water. They are often startled and fall into the water and drown. This is very unsafe for these pheasants, so a separate shed has been built for them. The other shed was built because the air in the eagle shed and the hibiscus bird shed was poor. A separate aviary was built to allow these birds to expand their range of motion and get more sunlight. In order to expand the zoo's operations, the zoo plans to purchase polar bears, rhinos, zebras, sea lions, orangutans, jackals, wolves, and other new and exotic animals. As soon as funds are available, the zoo will submit a request to the municipal government for approval to purchase them.

Public Actively Visiting

Recently, it has been the New Year, and many people have been visiting. According to the zoo's statistics, the number of visitors from January 1 to February 13 is as follows: 54,935 adults, 12,114 children, 252 groups, for a total of 67,301 people in January. On the 1st, 2nd, and 3rd of February, everyone was busy with the New Year, and there were few visitors. The 4th was a regular holiday and the zoo was closed. On the 5th (the second day of the lunar New Year), the weather was fine, and the number of visitors was particularly high, reaching 15,766. On the 6th, due to the snow, there were only 502 people. On the 7th, there were 8,942 people. On the 8th, there were 10,723 people. On the 9th, it rained again, and there were only 489 people. On the 10th, there was heavy rain and there were only 263 people. The 11th was a holiday. On the 12th, there were 7,901 people. On the 13th, there were 7,334 people. Yesterday, the weather was fine, and the number of visitors was probably over 8,000.

Collision of Small Boats at Pier No. 4 on the Bund

The Tianxiang small steamboat was damaged on Tuesday when it was crushed by a ship berthed at the same pier. According to the boat boss's report to the company, the damage was caused by the China Merchants Bureau's Feige ship. The Tianxiang sent a letter to the bureau to negotiate compensation. Yesterday, the bureau summoned the Feige ship's boss, who said that at about 5 a.m. on Tuesday, the Huangpu Beach Pier No. 4 was occupied by nine small ships: Yuguo, Mitsubishi, Huangpu No. 9, Shunxiang, and others. At 5:30 a.m., the sky was not yet bright. The Shunxiang ship suddenly left the pier without sounding its whistle. At that time, there were many ships and they were crowded together. The Shunxiang ship was forced out, causing the other ships to be squeezed. The Tianxiang ship was crushed, but it was not the Feige ship that caused the accident. The bureau sent staff to investigate and confirm that the Tianxiang ship was damaged, and the responsibility was not with the Feige, but with the Shunxiang ship that caused the accident. Yesterday, the bureau sent a letter to the Tianxiang, stating that the issue of compensation should be directly negotiated with the Shunxiang ship and had nothing to do with the China Merchants Bureau's Feige.

All Ships Should Strictly Prevent Theft of Machine Screws

The "Xin Feng" has already discovered it

The China Merchants Bureau's Northern Ocean Route "Xin Ming" vessel, on its way to Shanghai this time, discovered that screws on the rudder post of the engine had been stolen. Fortunately, the captain discovered it early and urgently ordered the ship's craftsmen to repair and replace them, so no accident occurred. Afterwards, the captain reported to the Bureau. Because the value of the rudder post nails is minimal, it is obvious that the thief had other intentions, and the loss of a single nail on the machinery can cause extremely great danger, which is of utmost importance to the lives and property of the entire ship. The "Xin Ming" ship's screw theft must be investigated. Yesterday, the Ship Department issued strict orders to all shipowners on all rivers and seas, starting from today, to carefully inspect all machinery parts on the ships, at any time and anywhere, to strictly prevent similar nail theft incidents as on the "Xin Ming" ship from happening again, to ensure navigation safety.

Shanghai Telegraph Office Extends the Regular Holiday Office Hours of Five Receiving Offices

Effective from this Sunday

Since the merger of post and telecommunications in this city on July 1st of last year, the number of places for receiving and sending telegrams has increased to more than thirty, making it quite convenient for merchants and the public to send telegrams. The Shanghai Telegraph Office, in view of the fact that the office hours of the post office on regular holidays are only three hours, has specially stipulated that starting from this Sunday (the 17th), the office hours of the receiving offices attached to the five post offices on Kaizi Road, Kade Road, Kade Road, Xiafei Road, Lima Road, and Jing'an Temple Road will be appropriately extended from 9:00 AM to 7:00 PM, without interruption in between, to facilitate the sending of telegrams by all sectors. However, outside the post office's office hours, senders must enter and exit through the side door or back door of the post office. In addition, the regular holiday office hours of the receiving office in the Postal Administration will also be extended in the shortest possible time.

Demolition of Beach Houses along Suzhou Creek

The Wusong River (i.e., Suzhou Creek) in Shanghai West, from behind the old racecourse, westward to the Fanhuangdu section, has not been dredged for many years, and sand has accumulated on both banks, forming beaches. In general, stores and residents along the river have occupied the beaches and built houses to live in. For several years, they have lived in peace, resulting in the river surface becoming narrower and narrower. Merchant ships from various villages coming to Shanghai often encounter blockages, cutting off transportation. Now, the Dredging Bureau has dispatched workers to start dredging, stipulating that the river surface should be widened according to its original width. Therefore, the houses along the river that occupy the beaches have been ordered to be demolished in recent days. When the project is completed in the future, the passage of ships will be unobstructed.

The Main Criminals in the Drug Manufacturing Organization on Xiamen Road Rescheduled for Further Interrogation

Female Criminal Yi Zhao Released Without Charge

The two major drug manufacturing organizations at Nos. 46 and 48, Zun Deli, Xiamen Road, accidentally exploded on the 8th of this month, resulting in multiple deaths and injuries. Only then did the police discover that it was a huge organization manufacturing heroin. The police successively arrested 15 men and women, including suspects Tang Jieyun and Chen Zonglian, at No. 53, Ximen Li, Ximen Road; No. 9, Houcheng Li, Mintini Road; No. 21, Tianle Fang, Xieqiao Road; and Room 317, Far East Hotel, Xizang Road, and escorted them to the First Special Court for interrogation. Therefore, detectives have been dispatched in all directions in recent days and stationed day and night in the above-mentioned locations in order to continue arresting accomplices. Indeed, the police arrested nine suspects in the above-mentioned locations in one day the day before yesterday, brought them all to the Lao Zha Public Security Bureau for detailed investigation. Among them, except for six who were found to be unrelated and released first, three more people, Zheng Zihua from Guangdong, Qiu Zhonghuai from Nanjing, and Chen Zhishan from Jiangbei, were found with several papers related to drug manufacturing on their persons. They were considered to be seriously suspected and ordered to be detained. Yesterday morning, Zheng, Qiu, and Chen were escorted to the First Criminal Division of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the previous situation, requesting permission to reschedule the hearing to Saturday to be tried together with Tang Jieyun and others, and stated that among the criminals brought to court yesterday, the female criminal Yi Zhao (i.e., the wife of lawyer Yi Qifeng) was found to be unrelated and requested that the arrest warrant be revoked and she be released first. After Chief Judge Qian verified the confession, he ruled that Yi Zhao be released, and Zheng Zihua and others be detained to wait for a joint hearing this Saturday.

A Girl's Corpse Discovered on Manchuria Road

Inside Lane 341, Manchuria Road, Zhabei, at around 10:00 AM yesterday, a girl's body was suddenly discovered. She was about four or five years old, wearing a blue striped cotton jacket, naked on the lower body, barefoot, without shoes. Both ankles were cut off with a sharp knife, with a total of four cuts. There was also a knife wound on the head. A murder weapon was left next to the body. For a while, onlookers were like a wall. Some said it was a kidnapping for ransom, others said the child had been ill for a long time and the family was angry and committed such a heinous act, and others said it was a superstitious and cruel act. They were born without raising, so after death, this inhuman act was carried out, cutting off both feet, so that this debt-collecting ghost would not be reincarnated again. There were various discussions. The incident was known to the patrol police, who reported to the Menggu Road Police Station. According to the instructions, the landlord Lu Abao was immediately instructed to go to the Local Court and report for an autopsy. After receiving the report, the court dispatched Prosecutor Zhao Chuanjia and others to conduct the autopsy in the afternoon.

The Second District and Fourth Branch of the Municipal Federation Held an Emergency Meeting Yesterday

The Fourth District Branch of the Shanghai Municipal Federation of Citizens of the Second Special District in the French Concession of this city held an emergency meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday. Eleven committee members attended, including Xia Shanxiao, Zhang Youmin, He Yaozhang, Zhang Lizhang, Sun Ruiting, and Huang Zhijin. Chairman Ye Ruizhai reported that a letter was received from member Wang Shunxing, Wang Lianqing, stating that four partners were playing mahjong for pleasure and were arrested by detectives from the French Public Security Bureau. The apprentice Wang Wenqing was also dragged out of bed, threatened by the Chinese inspector Qian Chenglong with a gun, and arbitrarily committed violence. He was then detained in the police station and forced to confess under torture, falsely accusing Dong Wenli, a standing committee member of the Federation, of opening a gambling establishment, hoping to falsely accuse the merchant. Although he was released immediately, the apprentice has been frightened and feels unwell. In this situation, how can the shop do business? Therefore, I specially request you to find a way to protect us. At the same time, Dong, a standing committee member, also reported in a letter about the search by the police and requested a negotiation. What should be done? Please discuss. After the committee members successively expressed their opinions, the following solutions were decided: (1) Send a letter to the police, firmly guaranteeing that Mr. Dong Wenli is a legitimate businessman and has no illegal activities. This time, Inspector Qian arbitrarily searched without any evidence being found and has been sending detectives to monitor him daily, which is illegal, depriving people of their freedom under French law. The French authorities should correct this and guarantee that the same thing will not happen again in the future. (2) Citizens gathering to play mahjong is a habit of merchants for leisure and is not prohibited by law. The inspector dispatched a large number of detectives to arrest people without the permission of the court or issuing a search warrant, which is even more illegal. Then, realizing his mistake, he immediately released them, going back and forth like a child's play, humiliating merchants to the extreme. Since there was nothing to be found, he arrested the apprentice and forced him to confess, falsely accusing Dong of gambling. A strict investigation should be conducted to reassure the business community. (3) Send a letter to the French Concession Taxpayers' Association, requesting the French authorities to respect the legal rights of citizens. In the future, if such incidents occur, a strict and thorough investigation of the facts should be conducted first, and the court should be consulted for a search warrant before execution. Otherwise, if there is no evidence from the court, it will be considered an illegal search, and citizens can refuse it to uphold the law. (4) Regarding the slander and insults suffered by the Dong Standing Committee Member and the member, they should file private lawsuits against the inspector in court separately. Next, the proposal to increase telephone prices again was discussed, and it was decided to send letters to the General Association of Taxpayers and other organizations to convene meetings to oppose it. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the area around Shandong is cloudy, the wind is turning to the north and is strong and sharp, and the Yangtze River basin and the coast here are overcast and cloudy with fog. This is due to the small low pressure being driven towards the coast by the high pressure in Mongolia. The wind conditions in the East China Sea are unstable, with times of gentle seasonal winds. The Taiwan Strait is clear. Also, the temperature in this city within 24 hours from 3:00 PM yesterday: maximum 56.8, minimum 30.4. The maximum was 50.2 and the minimum was 32.4 on the same day last year.

Educational News

The Ministry of Education Investigates Libraries Nationwide

(Nanjing, 14th) The Ministry of Education, considering that a survey was conducted on libraries nationwide seventeen years ago during the university period, and in order to understand the increases, decreases, and changes, specially issued investigation forms for libraries nationwide on the 14th, ordering national colleges above the specialist level and various educational halls and bureaus to quickly investigate and fill them out for compilation.

The Annual Meeting of the Geological Society of China Opened in Beiping Yesterday

Beiping, 14th The eleventh annual meeting of the Geological Society of China was held at the Geological Survey Institute in Pingle on the morning of the 14th at 10:00 a.m. A total of more than 50 directors, local members, and guests attended. Ding Wenjiang was blocked on the way due to a freight car derailment in Beining and failed to arrive in time. After the meeting, Chairman Xie Jiarong reported on the society's affairs, followed by Sun Yunzhu, the secretary of the conference, reporting on the loss of members in the past year and a half. Then, Qian Shengjun reported on the accounting, and Weng Wenhao reported on the editing and publishing situation. The entire body then observed a minute of silence for the deceased members to show mourning. After the adjournment of the事務 committee, the screening of films began, including the strata of the vast lands on both sides of the Yellow River Basin and the conditions in Ningxia. The performance ended at 12:00 and the meeting was photographed and adjourned. In the afternoon at 2:00 p.m., another meeting was held to read a total of seven papers, which ended at 5:00 p.m. On the morning of the 15th at 10:00 a.m., a lecture will be held at Peking University, with Weng Wenhao speaking on "Overview of Aluminum Casting in China" and Ge Lifu speaking on "Did Humans Originate in Asia."

League of Nations and Various Countries Plan Educational Film Cooperation

Notification of Resolutions from the International Educational Film Association

Seeking Ways to Cooperate with Various Countries in the Future

The International Educational Film Conference was held in Rome, Italy, in April 1934. Representatives from forty countries, including Britain, America, Germany, Italy, and China, attended, as well as representatives from the League of Nations Secretariat, the International Labour Office, and the World Intellectual Cooperation Organization. Renowned educators and film technology experts also participated. A key resolution of the conference was on the "International Mission of Film." The main points of this resolution were to raise awareness among governments regarding the international role of film as a means of promoting spiritual closeness and understanding between nations, as well as to clarify the material and spiritual lives of various peoples. The International Educational Film Association sent the resolution to the International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation of the League of Nations for review, entrusting the national committees on intellectual cooperation to assist in realizing the points listed in the resolution. The secretariat of the cooperation committee has notified the national committees on intellectual cooperation to liaise with the national educational film associations to collaboratively develop a public plan, hoping to achieve positive results from the proposal. The Chinese Educational Film Association appointed Zhu Ying, secretary of the Chinese embassy in Italy, as its representative when the International Educational Film Conference opened. The conference also elected our representative as vice president. Upon receiving notification of the aforementioned resolution from the League of Nations, it is planned to seek opinions from the preparatory committee of the Chinese Association for Global Intellectual Cooperation to proceed together. The resolution is recorded below: (1) The conference recognizes that the important purpose of their work is to make the mission of film a tool for cultivating public morals and knowledge, thereby enhancing mutual understanding between peoples.

The conference believes that film has an educational mission, and therefore, the responsibilities of film scriptwriters, producers, entrepreneurs, competent authorities, and all organizations or individuals engaged in the development of film are greatly increased.

The conference believes that countries should exchange educational films as much as possible, as this is a very effective method of enhancing mutual understanding between nations. Inspection tariffs and administrative restrictions should be reduced to the minimum necessary so as not to affect the principle of promoting exchange. At the same time, the conference also recognizes that inspection and administrative restrictions can prevent dishonest filmmakers and film merchants from producing films that provoke animosity between nations.

The conference sincerely hopes that governments will adopt all effective methods to promote the circulation of impartial films and strictly crack down on films that distort right and wrong.

In order to realize the above principles, the conference recommends that the Educational Film Association, in particular, adopt the following methods for consultants and specialized committees working jointly with the executive department of the World Intellectual Cooperation Organization in Paris: (A) Raise awareness among governments regarding the international role of film and its use as a method of promoting spiritual closeness between nations. Contact government authorities at any time to establish appropriate domestic measures or to negotiate specific opinions on international agreements, as well as conduct preliminary research to facilitate the drafting of formal clauses and submit them to the government. (B) Find ways to promote direct solidarity among film producers, such as through gentlemen's agreements, to encourage each other to produce fair and impartial films that have genuine cultural value and can enhance understanding between nations. (C) Collect and organize materials from various countries regarding film by establishing educational film bases or correspondents in various countries, or by establishing such organizations, in order to understand the material and spiritual lives of various peoples. (D) In order to achieve the above objectives, contact governments and all relevant international organizations at any time as much as possible.

First Collection of the Siku Quanshu Completed

(Nanjing, 14th dispatch) The first and second installments of the Siku Quanshu, commissioned by the Ministry of Education to be printed by the Commercial Press, were completed last winter. General Report on the National Labor Exhibition Evaluation (7)

Appendix

General Public Opinion on the National Occupational Labor Achievement Exhibition

Nearly 100,000 people visited this National Occupational Labor Achievement Exhibition. At the time and afterward, no fewer than a thousand people expressed criticisms and opinions, mostly from the academic and educational circles. Based on all the materials, the main points are summarized below for reference.

A. General Criticism

Most of the audience's comments were general in nature and can be categorized into three types:

(1) Praisers, (2) Dissatisfied, and (3) Skeptics.

(1) Praisers

1. The scale is grand, the works are exquisite, and such achievements are rare for a first attempt.

2. These achievements are the prelude to the development of production education and vocational education, and have already entered the path of linking life and education.

3. These achievements are greatly related to "nation-building and people-nurturing, and cultural revival."

4. The talent, strength, and spirit of our nation can all be slightly evidenced in these works. However, attention must be paid to the application and concentration of such talent and spirit, as well as their tempering and accumulation.

5. There are many national defense designs, which shows that the schools are quite capable of paying attention to national defense education.

(2) Dissatisfied

1. There are many toys and few supplies, many art pieces and few practical items, many entertainment items and few productive items. "There are too many things for decoration and appreciation by a few, and too few related to national economy and people's livelihood." There is no close adaptation to the actual life of society.

2. Most of the products inevitably fail to be "made without labor" or with very little labor, which is inconsistent with the purpose of labor.

3. There are many imitators and few inventors and creators.

4. The raw materials for products from various provinces and cities often neglect local specialties and domestic materials. They do not know how to use them, and even within the scope of local supply, they still purchase European, American, and Japanese materials, abandoning the near for the far, valuing others and belittling themselves. This is the mentality of national self-abasement.

5. The most lacking item in this exhibition is agricultural products. In addition, there are not many heavy industry, mechanical crafts, household affairs, educational supplies, metalworking, aquatic specimens, mineral specimens, scientific instruments, chemical crafts, working drawings, chemical military supplies, and the most common applications.

6. Labor products are mostly biased towards crafts, and the scope is very narrow. Those who do not know may suspect that this exhibition is a national craft product exhibition.

(3) Skeptics

1. Some of the achievements may not be entirely from students. Perhaps teachers worked hard, or workers acted as substitutes, or they were purchased from abroad.

2. Displaying counterfeit products and falsely labeling them actually loses the original intention of promoting production education.

3. To realize the true spirit of labor, one must start from not fabricating.

B. General Hopes

(1) Vocational Labor Education Issues

1. In the future, production education should be promoted, with production technology as the main purpose of training students.

2. In the future, the objects of labor should mainly be those that can promote national consciousness and spirit.

3. In the future, products should tend towards the daily practical applications of the public, so that school education and social needs can be integrated.

4. The mechanical industry should be actively promoted in order to coexist with other countries in the world of scientific competition.

5. The traditional manual teaching methods should be changed immediately. The teacher's responsibility is to guide students to create freely.

6. Vocational education emphasizes the results of production, while labor education emphasizes the work process. The purposes of the two should be clearly distinguished.

7. Courses such as embroidery and sewing should pay attention to work efficiency and application. Various labor projects should pay attention to economic conditions and should not cost too much money.

8. Achievements should focus on peacetime production, not preparation for exhibitions, resulting in ridicule of "temporary efforts."

9. Labor education in schools should be implemented seriously and should not be perfunctory, nominal, and ineffective.

(2) Advocacy and Encouragement Issues

1. The authorities should catch up quickly, work hard to advocate, and find ways to reward.

2. For the achievements of various provinces and cities that are close to people's livelihood and practical, statistics should be added, and methods should be guided and developed.

3. Those whose products are beneficial to society should be commended, permitted to manufacture patents, or exempted from taxes, or reduced their tax rates, to show promotion.

4. Provinces and cities that are perfunctory and irresponsible in this exhibition should be reprimanded.

(3) Establishment of Schools and Factories Issues

It is hoped that the government will expand vocational schools and manufacturing factories to cultivate talents engaged in production. However, the establishment of factories should precede the establishment of schools, which is in line with the procedure.

(4) Achievement Selection Standard Issues

1. The standard for selecting achievements should be strictly stipulated and designed by experts.

2. The works should be rich in educational significance and should focus on quality rather than quantity.

(5) Border Area Achievement Collection and Improvement Issues

1. In the future, the authorities should supervise the border provinces to pay attention to labor, and on the other hand, they should pay attention to the micro-collection methods, so that all places can participate in the products.

2. Subsequently, education should focus on remote provinces and should no longer conduct "hydrangea-style" movements in the prosperous areas of Jiangnan, resulting in deformed development.

(6) Product Control and Promotion Issues

1. Various special works should have unified methods to promote the whole country.

2. A national vocational school product company should be established in the capital, with a special labor material exchange office attached for research purposes.

(7) Teacher Training Issues

1. Statistics are needed for the required labor teachers, and a labor specialty normal school should be established.

2. Conduct labor teacher workshops or discussion meetings, and designate existing labor teachers to intensify training during the holidays.

3. In normal schools, pay attention to curriculum and teachers to cultivate talents suitable for assuming the responsibility of labor education. (End)

Private School Enrollment Declines This Semester Due to Economic Recession

Old Students Largely Absent Long After Semester Begins

Municipal Schools Remain Crowded Due to Lower Fees

Due to the economic recession in recent years, the number of students has gradually decreased. The semester has been underway for quite some time, but few students have registered at various schools. Our Shanghai correspondent has investigated the situation as follows:

Private School Enrollment Declines

It has been more than half a month since the beginning of the semester at private schools. Only two-thirds of old students have registered, especially at private secondary schools. Some schools have not even reached half of their enrollment from last semester. This is due to the difficulties of the rural economy and the fact that the Lunar New Year has just passed. Most students from the interior cannot raise the funds and therefore drop out of school. The enrollment of new students has also decreased, so schools are still continuing to recruit students.

Municipal Schools Remain Crowded

However, municipal schools still have full enrollment due to low school fees. Schools such as Wuben, Jingye, Xinlu, Wanzhu, He'an, Xicheng, and Shangwen are very popular. Each time they recruit students, the number of applicants exceeds the number of places by several times. Due to the limited number of places, those with aspirations can only regret their failure. The enrollment of mission schools has not decreased, because most of the students in these schools are children of wealthy families, so they are not greatly affected.

Shanghai Education Bureau Restricts Fundraising by Schools

Regulations Stipulated for Fundraising for Educational Donations

The Shanghai Education Bureau, considering that there are many schools in the city and fundraising is frequently heard, has, in order to prevent abuses, sent personnel to supervise and guide fundraising schools. Fortunately, no fraud cases have occurred. However, those who are generally unaware of the facts believe that there are no restrictions in the city's laws and regulations regarding school fundraising and proceed at will. It is too late when they are detected. In order to be cautious and thorough, the "Provisional Measures for Fundraising for Educational Donations in Shanghai" have been drafted and submitted to the Municipal Government for approval. The measures are recorded as follows: (1) These provisional measures are formulated in accordance with Article 7 of the National Government's Regulations on Commendation for Educational Donations. (2) All fundraising for educational donations must comply with the provisions of these provisional measures. (3) For all fundraising for educational donations, the reasons, methods, uses, amounts, and personnel involved must be presented in detail to the Municipal Education Bureau for approval by the Municipal Government before they can be carried out. However, if the school has not been registered or its performance cannot be considered satisfactory, it may not carry out fundraising. (4) The period for fundraising for educational donations may not exceed three months. During the fundraising period, every fifteen days, the fundraising situation and the names and amounts of the donors must be reported to the Municipal Education Bureau for record. (5) All fundraising for educational donations must be handed over to reputable banks for collection and storage and may not be used without approval. (6) Fundraising vouchers must use four-part receipts, with designated numbers, indicating the purpose and the name of the collector, and must be sent to the Municipal Education Bureau for prior stamping. (7) At the end of the fundraising, the names of the donors and the amount of donations must be published in the newspaper, and the register, receipt stubs, bank's notification of receipt of donations, and the newspaper publishing the receipt of donations must be submitted to the Municipal Education Bureau for verification. (8) If the donor has specified the use, the recipient may not change it. (9) The funds raised may not be changed from the original intended use and used for other purposes. If it is necessary to change, it must be reported to the Municipal Education Bureau for record. (10) After the fundraising period expires, the recipient must proceed with the approved plan, use, and progress within two months, and after completion, publish the use of donations in the newspaper. At the same time, a final account must be prepared, with attached receipts, and the newspaper publishing the use of donations must be submitted to the Municipal Education Bureau for verification. (11) These provisional measures may be amended from time to time if there are matters not covered.

Meeting of the Shanghai Boy Scout Council

The Shanghai Boy Scout Council held its fourth council meeting yesterday (the 13th). The council members present were Qu Yue, Luo Lie, Sun Yiming, Xi Yutong, Jin Xing, Zhao Weizu, Leng Xueqiao, and Yu Kuiyuan. Qu Yue chaired the meeting and Xie Yanbo recorded the minutes. The agenda was as follows: (A) Report Items: (1) The General Association approved the registration of the Bide Primary School Troupe, designated as Troupe 1150. (2) The General Association approved the registration of the Sisheng Middle School Troupe, designated as Troupe 1101. (3) The General Association approved the registration of the Hubei Middle School Troupe, designated as Troupe 1167. (4) The General Association approved the registration of 113 Dongya Boy Scout service personnel. (5) The General Association ordered that the Boy Scout curriculum and publications printed by Boy Scout troupes in various places must be submitted to the association for review and approval before they can be published. (6) The economic report of the General Affairs Department of the association. (B) Discussion Items: (1) Please amend and approve the organizational regulations of the Design Committee of the association. Resolved: Article 2 should be changed to "In addition to all council members of the council being ex officio members of this committee, the council will also invite 51 to 59 local enthusiasts of Boy Scout affairs, industry, and those with Boy Scout knowledge and experience to serve as members." (2) Please amend and approve the list of members of the Design Committee of the association. Resolved: (1) The vacancies of committee members Wen Hong'en and Shi Liangcai will be replaced by Shen Yi, Xu Peihuang, Wen Chaoji, Jin Xingren, and Cai Zengji as committee members. (2) All committee members who served as third-term council members whose terms have expired should be replaced by fourth-term council members. (3) The Shanghai Liangjiang Women's Physical Education Teachers College submitted a case for expanding the organization of the Girl Scout training class, requesting the General Association to instruct all levels of councils nationwide to send students to enroll. Resolved: Forwarded to the General Association as requested. (4) What should be done if the deputy instructors of each district of the association have not yet been fully appointed? Resolved: Instruct each district instructor to convene the troupe leaders of their respective districts as soon as possible and submit a report to the association for appointment before the end of this month. (5) How should the curriculum competition continue to be conducted? Resolved: The method of holding the competition by district will be re-drafted by the Examination Department. (6) Whether to hold the sixth city-wide inspection and camping event on a regular basis. Resolved: Change to holding it by district at the same time as the curriculum competition, and the method will be jointly drafted by the Instruction and Examination Departments. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Troupe Publishes Souvenir Booklet for the Completion of the Cenotaph for the Four Martyrs

Published on the 17th and Distributed to Guests

Soliciting Condolences from All Sectors Yesterday

The cenotaph for the four martyrs of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Troupe is scheduled to be inaugurated at 10:00 AM on the 17th of this month at the Shanghai Cemetery at the end of Songhu Road in the central district. Yu Zuoting, a fellow scout Bai Yechunian, will be the chairman of the presidium. Qu Yue and Xu Guozhi will be the chief and deputy commanders, respectively, and Wang Xiaolai will be invited to unveil the monument, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now heard that the troupe, in order to expose the enemy's brutality and commemorate the loyalty and bravery of the four martyrs, has published a booklet entitled "Photos of the Cenotaph for the Four Martyrs and the Stretcher Team." The content includes the circumstances of the four martyrs' martyrdom and the troupe's service during the January 28th Incident. The text is rich, and the printing is unique. All guests attending the inauguration ceremony on the 17th will receive a copy as a souvenir. Organizations that wish to request copies must attach a one-cent stamp. In addition, condolences from all sectors must be sent to the troupe at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce at Tianhougong Bridge before 5:00 PM on the 16th.

Shanghai Municipal Civic Education Center to Hold Speech Contest on the 17th

Held at the Center Starting at 9:00 AM That Morning

Hiring Hu Shuyi and Four Others as Judges

The Shanghai Municipal Civic Education Center has scheduled its first civic speech contest for 9:00 AM on the 17th of this month. The details are as follows:

Contest Rules (1) The speech time is limited to ten minutes per person. (2) The speech location is the center's lecture hall. (3) The order of speeches will be determined by drawing lots on the spot. (4) The evaluation criteria are divided into four categories: pronunciation, intonation, attitude, and organization. (5) The judges and participants will be divided into groups to evaluate the results. The top three who average the highest scores will be awarded prizes by the center.

Hired Judges The judges for the speech contest have been hired: Hu Shuyi, Yang Peiwen, Jin Guangmei, Tao Guangchuan, and Chen Ruizhi. A total of twenty male and female citizens will participate. The participation certificates will be issued by the center, and the participants must present the certificates at the time of the competition. Participants should pay attention to this.

A Glimpse of the Speech Topics The speech topics of the participants are as follows: Zhang Weisong's "How to Be a Youth of the Times," Jia Guanjun's "Saving the Country Through Aviation," Li Mujin's "Fascism and the Chinese Nation," Wang Huide's "The Way to Survive in the Future," Chen Ruiqing's "Political Power and Governance Rights," Shen Huan-cheng's "This National Way Out," and Du Jiaju's "Methods for Restoring China's National Status."

Recruiting Chemistry Talent

Since the establishment of the Career Introduction Department, the Chinese Chemical Industry Association has actively introduced chemistry talents to various factories and institutions to enable technicians to fully develop and promote the chemical industry. It is heard that the association has recently been entrusted by a well-known research institute in this city to recruit two chemistry researchers. Graduates of famous domestic university chemistry departments with relevant experience are qualified. In addition, one English typist is required, with the ability to type quickly and take notes. Those who are interested in applying can prepare a letter of recommendation, including their resume and experience, and send it to the Career Introduction Department of the association at 381 Bubbling Well Road, Shanghai, before February 28. After a review of qualifications, a notice will be sent to schedule an interview.

Recent News from the Shanghai Japanese Correspondence School

Reduced Fees for Enrollment

The Shanghai Japanese Correspondence School, located in the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society on Avenue Edward VII in this city, is divided into elementary and advanced classes. The elementary class starts with pronunciation instruction. The pronunciation lectures use three kinds of phonetic symbols, so that correspondence courses have the same effect as face-to-face instruction. The advanced class is prepared for those with some basic knowledge to continue their studies. Recently, in view of the poor general market situation, in order to reduce the burden on those who are interested in studying Japanese, a special fee reduction method has been set. This method is attached to the regulations, and the regulations will be sent upon request.

The Question of the Venue for the 1940 World Olympic Games

Meeting to be Held on the 20th of this Month

Rome, 13th (Havas Agency) - The current Olympic Games are scheduled to be held in Berlin next year. The next session is scheduled for 1940. However, Italy and Japan have both requested to hold the games in their respective capitals, so a decision has not yet been made. It is expected that this matter will be discussed at the Olympic Conference to be held in the capital of Norway around the 20th of this month, and member countries will be asked to use secret ballot to decide. Countries that do not attend will be asked to vote by correspondence. If the Norway conference fails to make a decision, a special meeting may be convened after the end of the Berlin Games to resolve the issue. According to reports, 1940 is the 2,600th anniversary of the founding of Japan, so the Japanese government has requested that the Olympic Games be held in Tokyo. Italy, on the other hand, has prepared to host athletes from all countries. An area in Rome is currently undergoing a complete transformation, with two swimming pools and a huge sports ground under construction. Italy has issued an official statement on the venue issue, stating, "Italy has not given up on hosting the 1940 Games. However, to show generosity to Japan, if the 1944 Games are decided to be held in Rome, it is not impossible to concede the 1940 Games to Japan, to serve as an embellishment for the 2,600th anniversary of the founding of Japan."

Spring and Autumn

Snippets

— (Jiaoxin)

The hole in an opium pipe, partially covered with smoke residue, is no bigger than a mung bean, but it can suck away all your wealth and reputation; even your life will eventually be buried in this hole.

A vibrant flower, inserted into your lapel by the hand of a florist, might at most cause you to sniff its fragrance. But if a beautiful young woman delicately pins it to your lapel, you would be overwhelmed and treasure that flower twelvefold!

The Catless Country

— Xunzi

I recall that twenty years ago, the Commercial Press published a fairy tale called "The Catless Country," which told of: "A country overseas that had no cats, so it was plagued with rats everywhere. Coincidentally, a Chinese merchant ship carried a cat, which the king bought at a high price."

Jingdezhen in Jiangxi Province is a famous porcelain production area. The "rat plague" there is comparable to that of "The Catless Country": "giant rats" weighing two or three pounds are not uncommon. As the saying goes, "rats cross the street in broad daylight, everyone shouts and beats them"—in Jingdezhen, rats walking on the streets during the day is considered "commonplace." Not only do people not shout and beat them, but they also can't beat them: because if you don't provoke the rat, it struts around as if it doesn't put people in its eyes. But when you want to find a weapon to hit it, it has already scampered away: so you can only watch helplessly as the streets are full of rats during the day. At night, it goes without saying, it is simply the rats' world.

It's not that there are no cats in Jingdezhen, but they are rare and precious. The price of a cat is not uncommon at one or two dollars: if you are not careful, the cat at home will be caught by thieves and turned into money! Therefore, one has to tie up the feline with ropes, causing the cat to lose its spirit after ten years of captivity, and its anger has long been thrown into Java. No matter how wildly the rats riot, the cat simply turns a blind eye and a deaf ear. In this way, having a cat is the same as not having one!

About "Selling Children"

— Zhang Huang

The business of trafficking in people is an ugly mark on human history. However, in years of famine and utter desperation, people willingly commit crimes and resort to aggressive means to survive. Besides, selling a child is like cutting off one's own flesh to heal one's own wounds. Although the law does not allow it, the situation is truly pitiable. When we hear the cries of "Selling children!" in the streets and alleys—especially on bleak evenings, in years of decline—who can fail to feel human sympathy and should forgive this behavior! As a certain gentleman from this newspaper described, pretending to sell children in order to cheat a few coins is also something that can be imagined and understood in the circumstances.

One day, I was chatting with my friend Mr. Liu Zixia at his home when we heard the cries of selling children in the alley. The servants and children all said, "This must be genuine, just listen to the desperate, trembling cry from the bottom of their hearts!" Several educated friends expressed their clever opinions: "This is a sham, right? It's acting so well to move people. How could they really sell their own children? They are just trying to get some money from people. Unless the children were kidnapped." Zixia, however, had his own opinion, saying, "There may be some who want to make a few more coins through this, or perhaps they are the majority, but they have no other clever tricks to use, so they have to resort to the moving pity of selling children; why shouldn't they be pitied? There are also those who really intend to sell their own children, because there are too many children, or they hope that the children can have a better future, or for other reasons. If they encounter such clever people—who know it's a trick—or such worldly people—who see through the deception—wouldn't that cut off their livelihood?" Everyone fell silent.

After that, whenever I hear the cries of selling children, I can't help but think of Mr. Zixia's arguments.

The Fate of Sheep

— Written by Shiying

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 9: Inept Flattery and Begging Lead to Scorn; Inability to Return Home, Seduced by the Guest's Exaggerations

Even though I am a man, you are two women traveling together, so it doesn't matter. I have hot tea there that you can drink a bowl of. I'll write a note and quietly send it to the Western restaurant in front to notify Mr. Cheng. Whether the matter succeeds or not, I'll give you a signal, which is much better than crying here. Although Mrs. Hu thought what he said made sense, she didn't know what kind of person Zhang Jiefu was and didn't dare to risk going. She didn't make a sound. Yueying said, "Okay, Mother, let's go to this old Zhang's house. I've met him before. You haven't eaten enough tonight, don't catch a cold." Zhang Jiefu said, "Yes, don't catch a cold. Even if Mr. Cheng refuses you, who knows, I can still think of some way for you." This sentence moved Mrs. Hu. She whispered to Yueying, "Shall we go?" Yueying said, "We can go. If Mr. Cheng says it's no good, we'll go back. It's late at night, what are we doing outside?" Mrs. Hu said, "Who isn't saying the same thing?" Jiefu said, "Okay, you don't need to worry anymore, just follow me." As he spoke, he was already leading the way, and he kept turning his head back to nod at them. This made Mrs. Hu and her daughter have no choice but to follow him. So Mrs. Hu supported Yueying's shoulders, following behind Jiefu, and walked to this small courtyard. Jiefu would take two steps and then stop for a while. After stopping several times, he finally led them into the house. Under the lamplight, looking at the complexions of the mother and daughter, Yueying was young after all, so she was still alright. This Zhu Mrs. Hu, with her hair disheveled on both sides, had a thin and gray face with tear stains. Her blue cloth jacket had picked up a lot of black ash from rubbing against the wall. Looking further down, the blue cloth pants revealed a few inches of small bound feet in thick socks. They almost looked like two stumps standing on the ground, where were the feet? (133)

The Fragrant Imperial Record

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Chapter 22: The Pear Garden Troupe

According to palace custom, although not explicitly stipulated by law, plays were usually performed on the first and fifteenth days of each month. Many of these plays were written by the Empress Dowager herself; originally, the Empress Dowager had a deep understanding of ancient Chinese dramas, and coupled with her considerable literary foundation, writing some plays was really not a difficult task! Performing plays in the palace was also considered a type of family entertainment, so except for major holidays such as New Year's Day, the Lantern Festival, and the Empress Dowager's birthday, it was rare to summon external performers into the palace to perform. On ordinary days, it was all handled by a group of eunuchs. They had also put in a lot of hard work and were skilled in many plays. The skills of a few outstanding talents were even better than those of outside performers. This was something that the Empress Dowager had long taken pleasure in.

Fortunately! The day after the Empress Dowager was saddened by her memories of Tongzhi, which caused the entire ancient palace to be shrouded in a cloud of sorrow, happened to be the fifteenth of the month, the day when plays were to be performed. Usually, on the day before the first and fifteenth, the Empress Dowager would mostly decide in advance what plays to perform the next day and give instructions. Moreover, the plays she chose were often just those few. These few were of course the ones that the old lady loved to listen to the most. She could listen to them repeatedly, five times, ten times in a row, without feeling bored. Naturally, the plays that she had newly written accounted for the majority! Therefore, people outside—including all the princes and ministers—never had the opportunity to hear the plays written by the Empress Dowager, while we few had heard them all so thoroughly that we could even recite the words. We were even tired of listening to them and couldn't wait for the Empress Dowager to stop selecting them again. Because the plays that we loved to listen to the most were still those old plays. These old plays were not only historically long-standing, but also had similar scripts in every troupe, only the dialects used by the actors were different. The reason why they could be passed down for so long and so widely was naturally because they had a kind of captivating appeal! (244)

Going to Japan (Part 2)

— Jiyun

The ship travels for fifteen hours to Nagasaki, stopping for three hours. We can then go ashore, enough for our investigation. Another twelve hours will take us to Kobe. The customs is nearby, so we can walk. After opening our luggage for inspection, we can take a train at "Sannomiya" train station to investigate industry in Osaka, visit the Imperial Palace in Kyoto, and see the culture of Nagoya, as well as the transportation facilities and commerce of Tokyo. There are many other places of interest, enough to give you a lot of gains that can be adopted after returning home.

You don't have to be timid. If you don't know the way, you can call a taxi. There are slight discounts, the cheapest being less than half a dollar. Rickshaws are very expensive, so don't even try. Who says Japanese vendors and rickshaw drivers are all honest? Don't be too superstitious, I've been cheated before.

When coming out for investigation, don't bring too much luggage, as shipping is very expensive there. One of my companions brought a steel trunk and paid more than six dollars for shipping, which is equal to one person's train ticket. Train shipping is calculated by weight, while shipping to a store is calculated by the number of items, about twenty to forty cents per item. Express train tickets and sleeper tickets must be purchased separately. Third-class cars have "water ting" flush toilets and "running water." Perhaps China will have them in ten years.

When you arrive in Tokyo, you can go to the YMCA and find the Zhang surname secretary. He can solve all your problems with food, clothing, shelter, and transportation. If you want to develop your career or gain new knowledge, going to Japan might be a good way.

Inheritance Inherited by Dog

Wealthy dog owners, out of love for their dogs, write down a bequest in their wills for their beloved dogs to inherit upon their death. These things often happen in European and American countries. Some even allocate huge sums of thousands of dollars in their wills for dogs to inherit. Not long ago, a rich man, also a dog enthusiast of course, bequeathed 200,000 pounds to his beloved dog in his will before he died. This kind of thing only happens in countries where there are too many dog lovers, right?

Small Recipes

Talking About Knife Fish

— Wan Gong

The best knife fish are produced in the lakes along the Yangtze River. The annual yield is very high, and they are all transported to Suzhou and Shanghai to be enjoyed by city dwellers. The fishermen of Taihu Lake, on the other hand, hardly get to eat any. This is as tragic as "those clad in silk brocade are not silkworm raisers." Knife fish have fine scales and tender flesh, rich but not greasy, and their deliciousness far surpasses that of shad and whitefish. If people were compared to fish, then shad would be mature, glamorous women, whitefish would be flirtatious, pretty maids, and knife fish would be young ladies just budding like cardamom tips: dignified yet lively, robust yet graceful, like sixteen-year-old girls.

Because its essence is particularly beautiful, it is extremely delicious no matter how it is cooked. Now, let me list a few cooking methods:

Steamed Knife Fish: Take a fresh knife fish, cut open its belly and remove the entrails, and rinse it slightly with water to remove the blood. Be sure not to remove the scales—because its flavor is all in the scales. Then, place it in a shallow porcelain pot with a lid, add some ginger, scallion stalks, a piece of raw pork fat, a few drops of cooking wine, and a small pinch of refined salt. Place it in a steamer and steam for thirty to fifty minutes. The heat should not be too high; if it is overcooked, it will become tough and stiff, losing its fresh flavor. This method of steaming is considered the best.

Braised Knife Fish: This is a common method. Although the flavor is richer than steamed, it has already masked some of its true taste. Therefore, experienced gourmets always prefer steamed.

Fried Knife Fish: This is a method for people who are afraid of bones. Use smaller knife fish, and prepare them in the same way as for steaming—cut open the belly, remove the entrails, and wash them slightly, but it is best to remove the scales this time. First, prepare a basin of beaten eggs and flour, and also prepare half a cent's worth of sesame oil. When the oil is hot, dip the fish in the egg and flour mixture, and then place it in the oil pan and fry until lightly golden. Because the bones have become crispy after frying, they will not get stuck in your throat. Although this method is fragrant and crispy, only two or three tenths of its true flavor remain.

Knife Fish Noodles: It is best to make them at home: use large, foot-long knife fish, steam them until cooked, gently peel off the scales, and lightly shake them with chopsticks. The meat will separate from the bones. If some small bones are still attached, squeeze them once more with a linen bag to remove them completely. Then, cook noodles with the original broth and the fish paste. That is truly delicious!

Knife Fish Rice: After opening and washing a knife fish, use three or four bamboo nails to nail it to the lid of the pot from its backbone. Cook the rice in the pot as usual. When the rice is cooked, lift the lid—be careful to lift it gently—and all the knife fish meat will naturally fall onto the surface of the rice. As for the bones? Because they are nailed by the bamboo nails, they are completely suspended on the lid and will not fall into the rice. This small pot of rice is full of knife fish meat and juice. When served, add seasonings and make it into rice soup. It can truly be called supremely delicious!

Gold Standard Gold in Turmoil

Lowest Price Seen at 918.5 Yuan

Several Twists and Turns Still Slightly Lose Six Jiao

Official Switching Starts at Three O'Clock Today

Securities: 96 Gradually Turning Around, 23 Customs Rally Breaks Out Again

Market Price Raised to 95%

Many Future Storms

Yesterday at the Chinese Securities Exchange, the 23 Customs rally was intensifying, related to powerful and organized manipulation. An investigation of the current month's deposit account showed over 2.2 million, the forward deposit account showed over 4.4 million, and the circulating amount outside the exchange was only 3-4 million. If the manipulators prepare funds to collect goods and the general holders are not short sellers in the market, then the short squeeze will inevitably become extremely intense. Even raising the price to face value would not be enough to offset the long and short positions, and there would inevitably be unexpected disputes at that time. This is the intention of the long positions. The short positions only know that the market price is high to face value, and anything above face value is illegal. An investigation of 23 Customs showed that the Central Bank only issued it, and it is said that the current inventory is only over 10 million, with the remaining 70-80 million scattered among various banks. Even if the manipulators are able to collect goods, they may not be able to collect any more in March, and the market price has already reached 95% of face value. Spot goods will naturally be released, which is the same principle as the US raising silver prices and China's silver outflow. It is now heard that powerful groups have requested the government to release spot goods to regulate the market or increase the amount of tickets to meet emergency needs. There are many rumors in the market, and no one can agree. Manipulation is undoubtedly occurring. Brokers have stopped new 23 Customs trading to prevent danger. Yesterday, the market opened with most bond markets being weak and spiritless. The 23 Customs continued to rise wildly, with the current month rising sharply by 1.8 yuan and the forward market also rising by 0.5 yuan. The manipulation was becoming more and more alarming. The 96 gradually turned around. In the second session, most of the short positions withdrew from the line, and new transactions were rarely concluded. Most bond markets rebounded by 0.3-0.5 yuan. The 23 Customs rose again by 1.4 yuan, with the highest price at 81.8 yuan, only 0.2 yuan away from the stop limit and 5 yuan away from face value. This wild state has been rare in recent years. Draining the pond to catch the fish, and the authorities are not preventing it, so there will still be storms in the future. As a result, most market prices rose by 0.1-0.2 yuan to 0.5 yuan, but the 23 Customs rose by 3.2 yuan, and the forward market also increased by 1.7 yuan.
