Free Talk

The Two Sides of Believing in Natural Forces

— Ling Mo

Although "modernity," in the terms of historians and anthropologists, is called the age of civilization and is the highest era of enlightenment known to modern people, distinguishing it from the age of barbarism, the physiology of modern people is almost entirely that of barbarians. The psychology of modern people, although more complex, if we admit that the barbarian's invention of ironmaking and the modern invention of changing elements are equally difficult, then we have little to boast about to the barbarians. The greatest effort the barbarians pursued was food, and the greatest effort we spend now is also in food and goods. The barbarians did not hesitate to wage war to obtain food and goods, and we often wage war now, and it is almost the same meaning.

Naturally, we no longer believe that war is ordained by fate. The display of celestial phenomena can be said to be where we differ from the barbarians. Neglecting the power of nature and fighting against nature is indeed something modern people can be proud of. But while we have partially been able to control nature by fighting against it, on the other hand, we have found that there are still too many places where nature is difficult to control. We still cannot help but be afraid of what disasters nature will give us. In this regard, we are not very different from the barbarians. Recently, someone said that the increase in sunspots will cause changes in electromagnetic lines and make people crazy, leading to war, which can be said to be this kind of psychology. But rather than saying that astronomers are trying to add a new explanation to the universally recognized inevitable war, or frankly mocking it as returning to barbarism and attributing it to fate, it is better to say that he discovered another place where "nature" must be controlled and is trying to control it. Because we are not all barbarians after all.

The achievements of the twentieth century in optics are indeed not small, but now it can only be said to be in the budding stage, so for some difficult-to-understand properties, there is only a feeling of mystery and surprise, and for its function, there are often speculative inferences that exceed imagination. Some of them are indeed based on reliable evidence. Now that we know that there is a kind of light (death ray) that can destroy life, then the question of whether there are other kinds of light that can affect human physiology will arise even in the absence of evidence. The claim that electromagnetic lines - or some kind of electromagnetic line - can drive people crazy is merely a fantasy of ordinary people, or does it have a scientific basis of its own? We cannot say until we know the details. But now there are people who want to discover a kind of line and use it to make people have psychological changes. If electromagnetic lines have this effect, then the effect of natural electromagnetic lines on life, even if it is very small, may be able to create a terror greater than the death ray when human power can control it. We do not believe that this will happen now. Perhaps it is not the smartest way, unless we are smart enough to understand light beyond the existing knowledge. We still do not know if there is anything external that directly governs the heart, but this problem will eventually be solved.

However, there must be a reason why the idea that sunspots affect human affairs is despised, because what the telecommunications transmitted has not added any novel reasons, but can be regarded as the resurrection of an old saying that is already dead. Former economists had attributed the cause of the economic panic that occurs about every ten years to the contraction of sunspots. We now know that it is only a cyclical coincidence, just as the "Napoleon's odd numbers" can be used to calculate the years in which Britain participated in the war as if. (See page 53 of the Supplement to the Shen Bao Monthly, Issue 30. The sum of the four numbers of a certain year used in it will not be less than eight or nine and will not exceed twenty-seven at the end of the nineteenth century. At the beginning of the twentieth century, it will be no less than ten and will not exceed twenty-one. Therefore, the number is probably seventeen or eighteen years, which is about the same as the interval between the two wars. Therefore, there may be a coincidence.) If this is really the case, it is naturally not credible at all. But we know that the appearance of the panic cycle theory was in the eighteenth century, when everything was believed to operate mechanically, and the cycle of sunspots had just been discovered, so there was such a novel inference. Now, although it is strange but not new, no one actually wants to revive it. But now there is a trend to believe that the quality points of light (usually still said to be waves) dominate everything, so talking about the influence of sunspots on human affairs is not talking about cycles but talking about electromagnetic lines. So this statement at least contains a background of the times.

If science is the religion of modern people, then it is inevitable that modern people will be superstitious about science with the same confidence that barbarians believe in fate. The actual reasons for wars between barbarians and civilized people are almost the same, but because the background is more complex, the explanation of this fate is also more complex than simple, and there is no other way except for barbarians to insist on their beliefs.

We Eight

— Ye Cao

We eight: Tu Er, Xiao Bing, Lai Wang, Da Xing, Hai Jing, Chun Shan, Mu Xing, and me, together, we are together all year round. Wandering, using begging to spend our days.

All eight are the same: together they are less than sixteen years old, have no home, and are all orphans. Once, Tu Er was fighting with Xiao Bing for a piece of rotten salted meat, and Xiao Bing cursed with uncontainable anger:

"I × your mother—Tu Er, you snatched mine!"

Tu Er did not curse back, biting his lower lip, jumped up with all his might, grabbed Xiao Bing and beat him hard. Everyone's advice was in vain. They tore at each other, beat each other, cursed each other, and fought into a ball. It was not until Xiao Bing's nose was beaten with blood that Tu Er let go.

In the evening, we eight, like eight stray dogs, huddled in a small corner. We have nothing, only using ragged sacks to house our hands and feet: the wind, like a cold snake, mercilessly drills into our sacks, flowing, making us unable to get warm all night.

We opened our eyes that are not often wiped, and peered at each other in the blurry night. Sixteen young ears were all listening to the somber sound of the wind sent over from the forest. Truly, because the history of our lives has lost its hope, we are even more thinking of our parents.

We are people from Jiao Village near Changchun. We eight have been together since we were young. Years of fighting destroyed our home. Our house was burned to the ground on that evening. Where are our parents? Only Heaven knows. But we eight are always thinking of them!

Wandering, the days of begging seem to have no end. Temples and abandoned houses have become our home. In the past, although our home was not very good, we had a kang in winter and did not worry about food. But now, we wear ragged clothes all year round. Except in summer, our feet and hands are always broken, flowing with that bright red blood.

We hate the Japanese devils to the bone. We are not afraid of him at all. We also hate ourselves, hate that we are too young and have no power. We are optimistic. We have not forgotten our hatred for a single day. We keep it in our hearts. We fight, we quarrel, but we will forget it the next day. Because of a scolding, we will become more intimate.

When Changchun was renamed Xinjing, we eight; together, set off for there. On the road, of course, we are still begging. Tu Er begged for two hot steamed buns and gave them to Xiao Bing first. Taking them over, this kid actually smiled.

We were kicked by the Japanese police and left Xinjing only after each of us had gotten many bruises. We eight stood there messily, then looked at those puppet policemen with eyes full of anger:

"When we grow up, wait and see..."

Symphony of Hutongs

— Hu Sheng

Living in an apartment in Beiping, one never feels lonely.

Previously, I lived in a small apartment where a gentleman in the neighboring room could sing famous songs like "Drizzling Rain" and "Peach Blossom River" by imitating a woman's voice. There was also someone who would open his mouth wide to sing roles from Peking Opera. However, since moving to this apartment, I haven't heard any singing or opera. It seems that the people living in this apartment are neither modern youths nor Beijingers. Because all modern youths should be able to sing "famous songs," and those who don't play stringed instruments or hum a couple of opera lines can't be considered Beijingers.

Although the apartment is quiet, living in it, one still doesn't feel lonely.

The sounds from the hutongs never cease. These sounds are completely different from the "city sounds" heard in Shanghai's garret rooms—the sounds of cars, trams, heavy trucks, noisy people, factory whistles… the kind that make your head swell.

Carrying items to sell, either pushing them in carts or holding them in their hands, peddlers travel from one hutong to another—these peddlers seem more numerous in Beiping than in the south. Customers can't be found inside the hutongs; they have to raise their voices so that people inside houses one or two courtyards away from the gate can hear them. Naturally, these cries are exceptionally loud and have long trailing notes. They are less inclined to use other tools, like the bamboo clappers or small gongs used in the south. Of course, there are those who don't rely on their voices, such as knife sharpeners who use a thin, arm-length horn that makes a wailing sound, monotonous yet extremely piercing.

Each type of merchandise has its own special phrases and tones. When I first came to Beiping, I could hardly understand any of these peddling cries. Now, although I understand a little better, there are still some I can't decipher. Or, even if I know what they're selling, I can only put "under consideration" what exactly they're shouting.

When reading or writing in the room, occasionally looking up, I hear one or two drawn-out cries, climbing over walls, passing through empty courtyards, and reaching my ears. The sounds might be "Roasted sweet potatoes... really hot..." or "Squeezed tofu..." or "Water chestnuts—sweeter than pears..."... Sometimes, several sounds alternate, echoing in the air. If the sound comes from a nearby hutong, naturally it's much softer, but it also seems especially distant. All the cries are so leisurely, as if sounds falling into empty cans—yes, the city of Beiping is like a hollow, large can, and these peddling cries just swirl and ripple inside this large can.

Those who sell roasted sweet potatoes push their carts, so naturally, they can only walk in the hutongs. But those who carry their wares in their hands, like those who sell what's called "candied hawthorns" in the south, can enter the apartment complex. They make a turn in the courtyard, softly calling, "Candied haws—rock candy." Don't think they can't shout loudly; once they exit the apartment gate, another cry of "Candied haws—rock candy" sounds much louder to you than when they shouted in front of your window. But the sounds gradually diminish; when the sound becomes very faint, you can imagine that they have finished walking this hutong and turned into another one.

There are also newspaper sellers who come to the apartment complex. Around eight or nine in the morning, an old man carrying only two or three newspapers walks into my apartment. He invariably says only three sentences: "Who wants a newspaper? Who wants a newspaper? Anyone want a newspaper?" After he says this if no one comes out to buy one, he quietly leaves. This is very different from the Shanghai newspaper boys who frantically shout "Want to read Shen Bao News..." in front of the Rising Sun Building. It shows a clear difference between the "Beijing style" and the "Shanghai style."

With such constant sounds as companions, one really won't feel lonely living in the apartment—although perhaps it's precisely because of these drawn-out sounds that people sitting idly in the apartment feel an emptiness and a sense of loss.

Because the apartment where I live is close to the main road, I can sometimes hear the sounds of cars passing by. On evenings when the wind is favorable, I can even hear the sounds of trams running from farther away—but once these sounds fall into the hollow, large urn that is the city of Beiping, they don't exhibit even a trace of urban atmosphere.

Mask

Altitude (4)

— (Henri Barbusse) Translated by Di Zhou

Thus, parallel to civilization, we fly through the night.

We, on that side of the black and gloomy space, looked far into civilization with giant currents of electric lights. Across the eternally dark veils, we flew over the zigzagging edges of shining Europe.

Through the telescope, cities appeared. Cities, at first, were faintly glowing lakes in the darkness, then turned into milky screens, and soon, soon became constellations. In order to distinguish the constellations of the sky, hidden at our fingertips, and superficially enumerated, we recognized the constellations by their Arabic patterns.

When flying at low altitude, the glossy, luminous planks of cities showed the same shape, even in the smallest parts. Paris, Berlin, Budapest, Vienna. All these cities looked like fireworks set off chemically on the ground.

Then we rose again into the "night" congealed on the hemisphere of the earth—looking down, we were astronomers of light, writing magnificent literature. We remembered the ancient Jehovah of legends, looking down at the stars from the heavens.

However, often, we overlooked the jewel-like signs engraved on many continents. These real names were completely forgotten, and we lost our sense of the aerial framework.

At night, we descended to the ground (along the edges of the constellation belt) from the center. From far away, they saw our point, saw a star penetrating among the many stars. Saw a star moving more slowly than the others. The light of the searchlight caught us. A tunnel of light. The light of the small lampposts made white stripes that divided the hemisphere of night diagonally. This white rope connected our place to the world of the full moon. When we stood on the ground and looked out, it seemed that half-black and half-white humans were moving on this surface of the lunar world.

Once again, we proceeded toward the sun, toward the surface of the earth, like a road covered with glory. This was also a wandering above the deeply slumbering reality, starting at night.

Looking out at this geographical sky, at the momentary flashes of interrupted emotion, when only a single planetary dot was searched for in the vast expanse of the universe, when we stood above it, we wanted to know: the things happening in the unclear places. We already knew those things. But at the same time, we also didn't know. We knew that every night, as the ceremony began, joyful transactions took place in the boundless darkness. We were sure that everywhere in all the cities where the germs of civilization were congealed, it was the same, and that in every place, human life was a prisoner's life. But this was only what the brain knew. Why, because the deep abyss of night also embraced the prisoners of the prison. Although night knows of the existence of people, it cannot see their forms. We wave our hands at what we cannot see and hold what we do not know in our arms. People want to lift the veil of darkness or want to get advanced words.

Soon, dawn approached. We walked along the gray latitude. The waves of vision galloped freely. From our bustling actions, the images of the fields appeared—the appearances of plains. Or the zones of land painted like openly unfolded oil paintings (farms), or the zones of thin and scabby filth (industry, mechanical rainstorms). Cities of whitened and blackened skeletal dregs floated up with violent inclinations. The strange city people thrown onto the streets from the morning... the people bound in the hell of the city—a dispersed, sandy crowd. Here, the monument to the war dead—the color of bones, the offerings of the rich. And there, the ugly bears of the rich were exposed and their drunken state was still in anger. Many filthinesses crawled in the small streets and alleys. But only the rational eye can see. We discovered and walked back. We had no leftover feelings and quickly passed through.

After a moment of shock, we quickly flew at low altitude. The eyes of the skyscrapers also touched us in a momentary darkness. In front of the high windows. Our vision flew swiftly into it. On top of all the equipment in the banks, in front of the vaults, behind the equipment for the mechanical setup of the offices, were pale people. A golden bull. That man was throwing the lines of the telegraph and telephone, like the silk of spiders. Above those collectives (above the glass windows) golden words were written.

—Jupiter (God of Heaven)

He chattered. But, what exactly was he chattering? (End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Common Etiquette Among the People

— Wan

In ancient times, after achievements were established, rites and music were created, calendars were corrected, clothing styles were changed, a model for a generation was established, and standards for governing the country were determined. Since the establishment of the Republic of China, military affairs have been pressing, leaving no time for administrative governance. Therefore, there are still no legal standards for folk etiquette and clothing. People act as they please and families follow their own rules, without a fixed framework.

Recently, the Legal Committee of the Legislative Yuan appointed Jiao Yitang, Peng Yangguang, and twelve other committee members to study the case of common etiquette among the people and convened meetings to discuss drafting methods. Thus, common etiquette among the people may soon be stipulated. Because without government regulations on etiquette, the people do not know what to do, either continuing the old customs of the Qing Dynasty, imitating the systems of Europe and America, or simply mixing old and new, combining Chinese and Western styles, resulting in a colorful variety that is bewildering. Therefore, the regulation of etiquette and clothing is a matter that brooks no delay.

Jiao stated in his report at the Legislative Yuan Memorial Week the other day that regulating etiquette can promote loyalty and filial piety among the people, and defining clothing can maintain national dignity. Indeed, the people of today pay too little attention to the words "loyalty and filial piety." The so-called duties of serving parents and respecting elders have completely disappeared. Promoting loyalty and filial piety among the people is a matter of urgent importance. However, what etiquette can express is only a form of formalism, and the spiritual promotion of it relies even more on the encouragement of education. In my opinion, common etiquette should be simple and easy to implement. For example, the old system of the Qing Dynasty can be said to have promoted loyalty and filial piety to the extreme, but its effectiveness is self-evident. Therefore, when stipulating the current etiquette, we should first reject all the previous hypocritical systems and replace them with etiquette that emphasizes spirit and practicality, so as to fully express the atmosphere of a new life movement.

As for the system of clothing, it is also necessary to consider it in detail. Our country has always been known as an ancient civilization, with superior national attire, wide robes and broad sleeves, and square steps and measured movements. If it is not like this, it is not enough to show the attitude of our great citizens. In the current trend, this kind of measured step, nose-wiping, and affectation is probably somewhat out of date. We should now promote martial spirit and a lively temperament, and should not promote rigid and corrupt life again. Last year, this magazine advocated a short-clothes life. As a result of research, the majority advocated that the clothes should be only about two or three inches past the knee, with a Chinese-style buttoned front. Recently, the clothing system of a certain province's New Life Movement is also similar to what this magazine advocates. Roughly speaking, they like convenience and fear being burdened, and their psychology is similar.

The current ordinary clothing system is either Western suits or blue robes and black jackets: completely Westernized, which is not enough to express our country's special etiquette. The blue robes and black jackets were also the formal attire of the Qing Dynasty's consultative council. This kind of clothing system is, on the one hand, not close to national conditions, and on the other hand, completely corrupt. It seems that neither should be adopted again. In the past, King Zhao Wuling advocated wearing barbarian clothes to educate the people. Now that our country is in a situation of military oppression, we should encourage and promote martial arts in order to save the country's precarious situation, so we should also pay attention to the clothing system.

The Art of Buying Used Books

— Rong

When you don't have money to buy books, even used books are good. In Shanghai, you can find countless used book stalls, and these places can often satisfy your not-so-extravagant desires. For example, if you go to North Sichuan Road, in addition to the fixed used bookstores, you can see many book stalls. A book of philosophy with a moralistic face can stand side by side with enchanting erotic series. Classical thread-bound books and imported crab-walking text can also become friends. These merchants don't know how to choose, and they won't choose. Books from ancient and modern times, from China and abroad, from the three religions and nine streams are all in one place, and nothing else can express the "Great Harmony Spirit" of treating everyone equally. They didn't organize them, but this is like a country girl who has a special charm in her plain clothes. It's also like wild trees growing naturally in the valleys, not like those in the park that are trimmed so flat as if they've had their heads shaved. There, you can search freely, and maybe you'll discover an erotic secret book, or maybe you'll get a banned book that you can't buy anywhere else. Sometimes, you can buy a famous foreign work for just a few cents. Sometimes you can guess the original owner's identity from the stamps, signatures, or even inscriptions in the book. There are many such book stalls in North Sichuan Road, Fourth Horse Road, and the City God Temple area. It is said that London has streets dedicated to selling used books, and several shops can put together a complete set of Shakespeare. The banks of the Seine in Paris are full of used book stalls with rare classical masterpieces. We haven't been to these places, but based on our own experience at the stalls, the taste is probably not much different.

However, buying used books also requires the art of buying used books, because sometimes the bookseller is very cunning. If you don't deal with them properly, you'll suffer a big loss or get angry and walk away, losing the joy of buying used books. I'm telling you, just the maneuvering around the book stall is an art. From there, you can understand the principles of being a person. For example, if you want to buy used books, you have to frequent new bookstores, know which books are out of print, what the prices of those books are, and which bookstores offer discounts. Most importantly, make yourself an expert. Then, you go to the book stall, see the book you want to buy or that is worth buying, and don't say stupidly, "Oh my God! This is exactly what I need!" You have to use your "skill." For example, you pretend to be indifferent and put the book aside. When you're about to leave, you seem to casually ask for the price, and if you say too much, you might as well sneer and put the book down, quoting a random price. However, the difference shouldn't be too great or too decisive, otherwise, the price negotiation will become unmanageable. The most important thing to note here is that if you like the book, you might as well linger by the stall for a moment, but don't walk away because the price doesn't match and then come back. That way, the market price might go up again.

Whether a book is missing pages or has stains should be checked before returning the price, otherwise you may suffer a big loss. But you shouldn't pay too much attention to the book, making it look like you love it too much, and let your opponent peek out your inner secrets. It's best to search in the corners, where there may be rich mineral deposits buried. I remember that I got an original edition of an aesthetics book and two copies of an American ten-thousand-book series book for my friend from those unnoticed places and exchanged them for a few cents.

The art of buying books is complicated. To make an analogy, this is like a bloody battle. Whenever you overcome your opponent, you can return triumphantly with a victory song.

Page 22

On Intelligence

— Hui Ren

Living in today's society, in the eyes of most people, is not satisfactory. The reasons are complicated, but in short, the vitality of life is somewhat lacking. According to fatalists, all of this is fate, because people are destined to suffer from birth, and the world is originally a sea of suffering.

But people are always intelligent and refuse to turn over in the sea of suffering and rush against the current. Needless to say, the wind is strong and the waves are high, even the tide of people running along with the suffering current is already surging like a mountain collapsing and the sea overturning, squeezing so tightly that there is not a single gap for you to pass through. If you are not swept into the seabed by the wind and waves, you will be flattened by the tide of people. It is not just drifting with the current, letting it fall, and besides the bitterness, there is no danger. Although the future is so long and boundless, compared to those who go against the current, it is much easier. So, intelligent people create an ideal world—a dream—outside of the real world out of the blue.

Dreams are indeed as free as can be. What you dare not do, you do; what you cannot do, you also do. The shortcomings of reality are all made up for in the dream. What is not enough, paint it; what is not perfect, change it. As long as you can think of it, you can plan all the restrictions of the system! There is no danger in this world, everything is free, unlike the restrictions in the current society. Looking up is a roof, looking down is a deep mountain; it seems that there, you are Jehovah, and you can control everything.

But putting it another way, the facts are always absolute, either positive or negative, and there is nothing in between. In short, one is a revolutionary warrior, and the other is a revolutionary traitor. Do you really want to create the victory in your dream from the failure in reality? You have to know that after the day, it is indeed the night; but after the night, it is still a day! Do you want to transcend yourself in reality? Humph, one times one is still equal to one.

Let me tell you, those who feel the pain of life's hesitation are not the coolies who are exploited every day, nor the capitalists who control the coolies, but the head-shakers standing by. They do not sympathize with the coolies who are sweating, but only worry that they will also fall into it.

Originally, removing the sweet illusion is even more terrifying; the smile in the dream is the source of bitter tears in reality.

If there is really a source of happiness in the world, it has to be excavated by human labor. If you want to dream of a source while sleeping in bed, it is too intelligent after all.

On the Yi River

— Chen Xuntao

Looking through the hazy smoke and dust in the airway, the Yi River flows like a snow-white silk practice from the gray horizon into the distant earth. The river tide slightly stirs milky white foam against the bleak wind of the northern country, like the fading white orchids on a widow's head, trembling and falling into scattered petals. Withdrawing his gaze, glancing around at the crowd of people in white robes who are seeing him off, in Jing Ke's eyes, they all seem to be mourners at his funeral, grieving for him. Their faces are all solemn and melancholic; especially Gao Jianli, the heroic spirit of singing with sorrow and generosity when drunk in the Yan City market, has also become desolate at this moment.

Jing Ke feels that this trip is too risky. He complains about Prince Dan for just this point. It is somewhat reckless to take the callow Qin Wuyang as his deputy, and go deep into the ferocious and powerful Qin with a short dagger. He believes that Prince Dan does not have a calm mind, a careful long-term vision, but is just a mediocre person whose emotions have surpassed his reason. He wholeheartedly wants to vent his anger for the Yan State and the weak vassal lords, but how has he considered the tyranny of the King of Qin, the ferocity of Wang Jian? The immaturity of Qin Wuyang, and even what unfortunate results will come of this trip, he has not even considered. Although Jing Ke, who has always prided himself on being generous and heroic, cannot help but feel sad about this in his heart!

Before his eyes, the vast Yi River connects to the sky, and the bare branches and trunks of the flat forest stand upright. A bleak view of desolation and decay... From now on, it will be farewell forever! Recalling the countless taverns in the Yan City, the places where he used to sing and weep with Gao Jianli and the dog butchers, he will never go there to look up and down and linger again! Raising his eyes and looking at the road ahead shrouded in smoke and dust, Jing Ke's vision was suddenly covered with a layer of hot, tearful moisture, and everything blurred past.

Scattered fallen leaves rolled up gently with the wind, and then ran wildly away. Grief came from Gao Jianli, and as soon as he hugged his zither, his hands were already trembling with excitement. Soft and pliable bamboo was drawn across the strings, involuntarily forming a changing tune; and Jing Ke's sorrowful singing was also filled with the endless sadness of life and death, the sorrow of leaving the country. Not only this crowd of people in white robes seeing him off, looking at each other sadly, wiping away a sympathetic tear for Jing Ke. Even the bleak cold wind was crying for him, and the sentimental fallen leaves used a rustling vibrato to mourn the sorrow of his future!

Jing Ke's singing voice was already choked up and he could not sing. Gao Jianli's zither sound suddenly turned from poignant to generous and solemn. Everything was silent, only this resolute sound powerfully stirred everyone's hearts, so solemn that no one dared to shed a cowardly tear.

Jing Ke slowly raised his head in extreme thought, his eyes making a tour around. He saw Prince Dan's doubtful and eager expression, Qin Wuyang's contemptuous gaze, and even the people seeing him off who had just sympathized with him, seemed to be secretly laughing there;

"Jing Qing is such a coward! Wang Jian's beast army is only separated by the Yi River, but he is shrinking back, avoiding it. Look at Qin Wuyang, this child, how brave he is! More bloody and more resolute than him!"

This was truly a great insult to Jing Ke. He hummed in his throat with self-confidence. His whole body trembled from excessive excitement, his protruding eyes burning with fierce anger, suddenly swinging his iron-like fist and hitting the air violently, opening his throat and shouting, roaring like a lion:

"The wind is soughing, the Yi River is cold, the hero goes forth, never to return!"

The voice was high-pitched and loud, reaching the blue clouds, and everyone's faces were so moved that they changed from melancholy to stern iron blue. The wind was howling, and the Yi River was surging with violent waves, as if the spirits of the great and magnificent rivers and mountains were also responding轰轰烈烈 with great enthusiasm.

Jing Ke took the two gifts: Fan Yuqi's head, this hated fugitive's head, trembling, and the Dukang map with a cold dagger inserted in it, patted Qin Wuyang's arm, and said:

"Let's go!" So resolutely.

The silhouette of the carriage had already disappeared in the distance. Prince Dan and the others, the group of people in white robes seeing him off, were still smiling as they watched the tracks of the carriage on the avenue. They were waiting for the tragic drama of the assassination of the warmonger to be staged in the Xianyang Palace when the dagger was revealed at the end of the map.

From Inland Attacks to the City

Ginza Nights

— Qian Hong

Ginza is the most bustling area in Tokyo. Therefore, any friend who comes to Tokyo knows that there is a place called Ginza and wants to take a stroll there. When I first arrived in Tokyo, I didn't mind the hard work and went to Ginza once.

It was a night with a hazy moon. Mr. Chen, the "old Tokyo-ite," and I strolled from Waseda to Hibiya, and then from Hibiya to Nihonbashi, and then to Ginza. Once in Ginza, the hazy moonlight was nowhere to be seen, replaced by the dazzling electric advertisements that crisscrossed the space like nets. Several major department stores, including Shirokiya, Matsuzakaya, and Mitsukoshi, were all concentrated here. The Japan Theater and Tokyo's most famous cafes and dance halls were also all here. Walking through such a lively area, it was just the time when the night market was opening. The roads were naturally filled with cars and horses, coming and going endlessly, and the sidewalks on both sides were as crowded as during temple fairs in the countryside. In the middle, separated from the roads and sidewalks, were rows of night market stalls. On these stalls, there was everything from daily necessities, food, toys, books, and night clothes to antiques. Although the goods were no different from those sold in companies or shops, the prices were more than 20% cheaper. Therefore, people living in Tokyo all knew the benefits of going to the night market to buy things, and they weren't afraid of the crowds and came to the streets when the night market opened. We walked slowly, like country bumpkins entering the city for the first time, carefully observing everything. We learned that no matter what they sold, they used practical experiments to advertise. For example, if you bought a newly invented compass or a water pipe connected to a tap at a stall, the stallholder would tell you in detail how to use it and show you the results of the experiment. This was indeed a very good business method. When we turned onto the left sidewalk from Shinbashi, in that corner stood two young men with artist-like hair, trying to sell us their works. Ah! So these were the street artists I had often seen in books. Driven by hunger and cold, they came to the streets to sell their art at extremely cheap prices. Among the few portraits hanging there, I recognized one of Kan Kikuchi. Although the painting technique wasn't very skilled, the brushstrokes were very lively. The portrait of Kikuchi Kan was also very lifelike. Therefore, I spent ten minutes and two jiao to have them draw a quick sketch of me, and then bought a frame from another stall. In total, it only cost me five jiao to get such a perfect thing, which I could never get in Shanghai. Finally, Mr. Chen took me to one of the largest tea houses, where I drank a cup of coffee and feasted my eyes on beautiful scenery. Only then did I leave Ginza with a tired body and an excited heart.

Amateur Mailbox

What is My Ambition?

Editor:

Although I have never met you, I often see your correct answers in the newspaper, which have long made me admire you immensely.

I now have a few questions that I would like you to explain to me. Let me first describe my situation: My parents are both alive, both over fifty years old. I have two siblings, and we make a living by farming to support the family. After graduating from elementary school, due to financial difficulties, I was unable to continue to middle school, so I had to leave my books and enter this dark society, hoping to acquire a skill to comfort my parents' high expectations. I am now working as an apprentice, earning nine yuan a month. From this small amount, I also have to supplement the family expenses, so my finances are very tight. However, I am not discouraged by the difficult environment; I want to strive forward. I think that a person standing in society cannot live solely for the sake of bread; at least they must seek some benefits for society and some happiness for the country, only then is there meaning. Therefore, I want to take advantage of this vigorous time, using my brains and sweat, to work hard according to my firm ambition. However, in my heart, I don't know what my ambition is? How can I achieve my goal? Therefore, I am writing to you, earnestly asking for an indication to lead me towards a bright future. At the same time, I was born in this era of frequent disasters, driven by the environment, various contradictory thoughts are spinning in my mind all day long. I often wonder what kind of ideology is needed by China? This really makes me extremely bewildered. I think you are knowledgeable and experienced, and you will surely give me a clear explanation! Respectfully,

Xu Xing

Editor's Note: It is commendable that you can have a positive and enterprising spirit in a difficult environment.

You said: "A person standing in society cannot live solely for the sake of bread; at least they must seek some benefits for society and some happiness for the country." This is very true.

You want to take advantage of your vigorous time, using your brains and sweat, to work hard according to your firm ambition: but you yourself do not know what your ambition is, so you do not know if you can achieve your goal. These words are not correct. First, a person's ambition must be found in society. Relying solely on inner fantasies will not lead to any correct ambition. Second, you yourself "do not know what my ambition is," then how can you "work hard for a firm ambition"? What goal can be achieved?

You also said: "I often see your correct answers in the newspaper, which have long made me admire you immensely," "earnestly asking for an indication," "lead me towards a bright future." Here, I want to advise you: do not blindly believe in me, just as you should not blindly believe in any individual. If my words make sense, then believe in those principles; blindly worshipping an individual is a very dangerous thing!

Now is the time when theories are divergent, and it is also the time when everyone is trying to find a way out for China, and it is even more so the time when the whole world is finding a way out in panic. Nothing has reached the final stage, so at present, if you ask me what ideology is needed by China, then I cannot answer you.

However, you yourself should work hard to study this question, because you yourself also have a method to answer this question. This best method is to open your eyes and investigate the facts of society. Whichever ideology is compatible with the facts, then that ideology is what China needs. Using this method, not only will you be able to get a very correct answer in the future, but the majority of the Chinese people, undoubtedly, will also get the same answer in the future. Because there is only one fact, and there will only be one answer in the future.

But you should not rely solely on your personal naked eye to determine everything, because what the naked eye sees is sometimes just a superficial appearance of reality: and relying solely on personal investigation is also limited. Therefore, you should also read more books. At the same time, you should also study the process of social development and grasp the important points of current society. In this way, your ambition in the future will definitely be very firm and very correct, and your goal can definitely be achieved.

Classical Chinese

Feng Mingquan National Studies

Zhongxi (1040) 8:00 AM to 9:00 AM

Yang Yun's Letter to Sun Huizong (2)

1:00 PM to 2:00 PM "Mencius's Utmost Heart" Chapter on Not Eating Idly

Sun Deyu University

Hangyun (1180) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Those in ancient times who wished to manifest their clear virtue throughout the world first governed their states. Those who wished to govern their states first regulated their families. Those who wished to regulate their families first cultivated their personal lives. Those who wished to cultivate their personal lives first rectified their hearts. Those who wished to rectify their hearts first made their intentions sincere. Those who wished to make their intentions sincere first extended their knowledge. The extension of knowledge lies in the investigation of things.

To manifest clear virtue throughout the world is to enable all people to have the means to manifest their clear virtue. The heart is what governs the body. Sincerity is truthfulness. Intention is what the heart manifests. To make the heart's intentions truthful is to desire that they are always satisfied and without self-deception. To extend is to exhaust. Knowledge is understanding. To exhaust our knowledge is to desire that what we know is all-encompassing. To investigate is to arrive at. Things are events. To exhaust the principles of things is to desire that no extreme is left unreached. These eight are the items of the Great Learning.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

London, the World Film Center, Will Replace Hollywood

— Chen Xiong

I once told readers in this publication that British filmmakers had officially launched an attack on the United States, seeking to open up theaters in major American cities. Now, a year later, British films have not only established a solid foundation in the American market, but London, the production center of British films, is poised to become the world's film center, replacing the authority of Hollywood, the only film city for decades.

In the past year, the rapid progress of the British film industry has been more significant than in the previous twenty years. After several years of desperate struggle, British productions have achieved great success in the American market. George Arliss—one of the best actors in Britain—shone like a shooting star, suddenly acquiring the qualification for the highest salary of Hollywood actors and appearing on the British silver screen. The completion of his latest British production, "The Iron Duke," made American filmmakers pale in comparison. When the salaries of British actors can be equal to those received by Hollywood, it can prove that British filmmakers have sufficient economic preparation to compete with Hollywood.

It is not surprising that George Arliss—an artist qualified to be elected to the Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences—was recruited by British filmmakers. What shocked the American film industry the most was that Hollywood's top director Ernst Lubitsch was also recently lured to Britain. Lubitsch's reputation warrants the British film industry's considerable appeal to lure this talented director. Now that the best actors and the most famous directors in the United States have come to the British silver screen, there is no choice but to have bright prospects for the future development of British films.

These two famous figures in the film industry will all take London as the base for their development, and it is expected that they will add a unique color to the British film industry. Due to the precedent set by Arliss and Lubitsch, perhaps many American stars, directors, photographers, screenwriters, and other talents will jointly join the British film industry. At that time, British filmmakers will truly be able to be proud for a while. Now, American production companies, seeing the current situation, are all surprised by the new situation of the British film industry's courage and progress. The proud attitude of looking down on British films has now changed to admiration and suspicion.

Currently, at least ten British film companies are releasing their productions around the world, while the American film industry, which has always been dominant in the world film industry, has only eight major film companies. London's "The Private Life of Henry VIII" and "The Rise of Catherine the Great" are both works that have caused a sensation in the world film industry in recent years. Gaumont's "Man of Aran" is the British work that won the championship at the recent International Film Exhibition in Rome. There is also a "Chu Chin Chow," in which Chinese actress Anna May Wong participated in the performance, and is now being screened in New York's largest cinema, and is the masterpiece of the Gaumont Company. On the day of the premiere, President Roosevelt personally visited and praised the British work. Until recently, "Chu Chin Chow" was still a sold-out show in New York, so other city theaters are impatiently waiting for the British film to be screened in their area.

The British film industry is also working hard on publicity. Currently, the largest advertisements in American newspapers and theater advertisements are for British films. When Gaumont Film Company began setting up distribution offices in the United States last year, it ran several issues of color page advertisements in the most widely circulated film publications in the United States. This was a precursor for the American film industry to feel that its territory had been diligently sown. In the past, newspapers did not publish news about British films. Now, British film reviews, photos of British stars, and news about the British film industry are all materials that American newspapers like to publish.

Hu Die's performance in this film is quite successful, portraying the elegance of Ren Zhu as a young girl and the dignity of her as a young woman. The performance of Cui'er, the uneasy maid, and the kindness of Madame Youlan are all very successful. Gao Zhanfei's performance is not special, but he is dutiful. Xuan Jinglin maintains his past achievements, and Yan Yuexian's performance is very outstanding.

The sound and photography are clear, the lighting is perfect, and the shots are lively.

My Thoughts on "Orchid in the Valley"

— Zhou Hui

First of all, I should say that the clarity of the pronunciation and the fluency of the dialogue in this film are rare in domestic films.

The director does not have anything particularly commendable here. He simply presented the performance in a straightforward manner, without any lightheartedness, briskness, or compactness. There is no talk of film art techniques here. However, the interspersed gimmicks have harmonized the overall sad atmosphere quite a bit, and this is quite an achievement.

There are two points here that are confusing: (1) Where did Rouyun's murder weapon—the pistol—come from? It was not mentioned on the screen and came strangely. (2) Ji Lansun was originally a revolutionary who participated in the Northern Expedition, but later he was just a young man who talked about love and indulged in pleasure. The personality is too contradictory before and after.

In terms of actors, Hu Die is average. She is competent in playing the graceful and wealthy Ren Zhu, and her lines are also lively. Gao Zhanfei has nothing to commend. Yan Yuexian is very successful. Xuan Jinglin did not disappoint either.

As for the few songs interspersed in the film, they can be said to be superfluous and unnecessary. The photography is average. The set is very gorgeous.

The Interweaving of French Law and Love in "A Scandalous Affair"

— Yunmen

Shouldn't the responsibility of a lawyer who protects human rights be to strive for fair legal sanctions for the weak who have been wronged, and to exhaust his intelligence in defense? Should a beautiful young woman enjoy the right to youth and seek affection? Should an unfortunate girl sacrifice her chastity and money for the sake of great love? If that lawyer, due to business relations, throws himself into the inescapable net of a romantic wealthy woman and becomes her prisoner of love, and at the same time discovers that the main culprit in a certain case is his own beloved wife, then what should he—the human rights protector—do? If that passionate young woman, unable to withstand the temptation of spring, blindly abandons her family and reputation, seeking a like-minded partner, and discovers that he is a rascal who extorts money, then what will she do? And if that girl, after her reputation is ruined and her money is exhausted, realizes that her lover is just a vampire, then what can she do? These are all unsolvable problems in "A Scandalous Affair." However, murderers die, and there are constant punishments in the law. Wives who are unfaithful and husbands who are disloyal are also rejected by public opinion. How much benefit do parasites who rely on selling love take?

William Powell and Myrna Loy, in response to repeated requests from the audience, co-starred in this "A Scandalous Affair" through the efforts of MGM. William Powell and Myrna Loy are a pair of on-screen lovers who are considered the most suitable and satisfactory by the audience. Therefore, his and her first production, "Manhattan Melodrama," received extraordinary praise, and the second collaboration, "The Thin Man," changed the style of detective films. At the same time, the success of their collaboration also laid a solid foundation. Sure enough, the third collaborative film "A Scandalous Affair" was released. After seeing such a bizarre and tortuous plot, we certainly trust his and her talents and determine that it can surpass the previous work and satisfy the eager desire of our movie fans.

Review of "Three Heroes of the Barren Desert"

— Ling He

Ｔhe　Three　Musketeers

——Paris

After watching this film, I am almost speechless. On one hand, the so-called martial arts films are ultimately tiresome. On the other hand, the film itself is very empty. We cannot demand substantial content from every film, but this film, besides showing imperialist soldiers jokingly killing people in the colonies, hardly presents a complete story. Otherwise, if there is a story, then due to the chaotic weaving and the immature presentation methods, it fails to give us a relatively unified impression.

As a martial arts film, "Three Heroes of the Barren Desert" gives people the impression that the horsemanship is very good, and the several fight scenes are also very realistic. However, what I want to talk about here is not these, but the scenery in the desert. The fierce battle at the beginning of the film seems quite vivid, but that's just about it. Later, it just develops with Cut Cut, and the story is not narrated very clearly.

If we study Montage, the Cut o Cut of the silent film era often evokes our memories. Nowadays, due to the progress of expressive techniques, people have mostly forgotten that method. Therefore, although "Three Heroes of the Barren Desert" also uses very few "wipes" and Dissolves, it still attracts our attention. However, it hasn't even managed to narrate the story clearly, so there's nothing else to talk about.

Audience Opinions

Thoughts After Watching "Orchid in the Empty Valley"

— Yu Bi

From the perspective of editing techniques, this film has eliminated a lot of verbosity compared to the previous "Orchid in the Empty Valley," and of course, the performance is much tighter. However, some places are not very clear, such as Lan Sun's return from the battlefield to Ren Zhu's house, which is not shown in detail on the screen. Rou Yun and Ren Zhu walk from the bedroom to the hall in the middle of the night, passing through many doors, and the sound of closing the doors is very loud. Could it be that none of the many servants in the Tao family are aware of it? When Rou Yun commits suicide, and Lan Sun hears the gunshot, wouldn't he open the door to take a look?

The director's techniques are very flexible, and there are many clever tricks, such as tearing off the calendar pages one by one to indicate that the days are passing by. The different performances of the clock indicate the amount of time Ren Zhu spends on makeup. Several close-up shots are very conscious.

Film Novel

David Copperfield (9)

— Liu Cun

After David's Dora died, he was utterly disheartened. A year of traveling might enable him to forget his pain and restore his old mood. But in fact, he returned to Canterbury, where the situation had been messed up by Uriah Heep, and Micawber himself was also entangled in it. The formerly optimistic Micawber, according to Mrs. Micawber, was on the verge of madness. His previous amiable temper had also disappeared. Whatever he thought about, he thought about Heep; whatever he said, he said Heep. But finally, as a result of the advice of David and his aunt Betsey, he told everything he knew and decided to eliminate Uriah from their lives.

Once they had decided on their plan, they besieged Uriah one day and launched an attack. The only weapon they held was a statement of Uriah's crimes, written by Micawber himself, which began with: "I have to declare the crimes of the most unprecedented villain in the world, and I can no longer care for myself. Humility, poverty, and disappointment have always been my lot in a life of suffering. Now, even if I am bound by ropes, I must declare that Heep, none other than Heep, is a forger and a fraudster."

The paper also described how Uriah had tricked Wickfield into signing seemingly unimportant things, which were actually important documents. Uriah used this method to withdraw trust funds for his own use and forged Wickfield's name on many other registers. He used every means to subdue Wickfield and Agnes.

Uriah, attacked by the crowd, was initially furious, reversing his usual humble attitude. Later, David forced him to hand over the shareholder's deeds for destruction. Uriah still refused to give in. David also told him to hand over all the embezzled funds, or he would immediately call the local officials. At this point, Uriah had no choice but to yield. He obediently handed over the shareholder's deeds and the embezzled funds, one by one, because he knew that all the evidence of his forgery was in Micawber's hands, and if he alarmed the authorities, he would have no hope of escape.

After Uriah Heep was expelled, Micawber set off for Australia with his family. On the day of their departure, David, David's aunt, Peggotty, and others saw them off at the dock. Micawber was in high spirits, wearing oilcloth clothes for the voyage and a telescope hanging from his chest. Mrs. Micawber and her children were all dressed like pioneers of a new world. Micawber stood at the bow of the ship, bidding farewell to the people who were seeing them off, saying: "We have abandoned the luxury of our homeland to open up a new world, and we are ready to become new citizens of Cai Tian Xi Di!" He turned to David and thanked him for all his help. Soon the ship set sail. Old fisherman Dan Peggotty, Mrs. Gummidge, and Miss Murdstone were also traveling with the Micawber family. Although it wasn't as happy as before, they were still reunited.

A few days later, David and Agnes were walking on the hillside by the coast, on their way to visit Aunt Betsey. David suddenly said to Agnes: "Now, in this utter silence, and in the face of this beautiful, picturesque sunset, I want to say a few words to you with all sincerity. I want to tell you—when I left you, I loved you, and when I was away from you, I also loved you, and now that I have returned, I still love you." Agnes said softly: "David, do you remember the night that Dora passed away, when the two of us were together? The last thing she asked of me was to take a place in your heart for her. I have loved you dearly all my life." The two of them stopped, and in that moment, everything was forgotten—all the characters that decorated David's life, all the poverty and pain, and even the people he had loved, had all disappeared, leaving only himself and Agnes, standing face to face on the cliffs of Dover, the waves crashing against the shore at their feet. (The End)
